<article id="post-319" class="group post-container">
	<header class="entry-header">
		<h1 class="entry-title">Ph.D. in Performance Studies: Admissions</h1>
	</header><!-- .entry-header -->

	<div class="entry-content">
		<p><strong>Application deadline &#8211; December 1, 8:59 pm (PST)</strong></p>
<p>Dear Prospective Student:</p>
<p>We are delighted by your interest in the Ph.D. Program in Performance Studies and hope you will find the website materials helpful. Our program is an unusually flexible one, designed to prepare students for advanced research in the field of performance studies. As you know, the program at Berkeley draws its strengths from a Graduate Group of faculty in disciplines ranging across a host of fields and departments. We encourage students to take the initiative in developing a program of coursework that will lead both to a solid command of a given field and to the kind of interdisciplinary research characteristic of the strongest work in performance studies today.</p>
<p>Although it&#8217;s certain that your interests and plans will evolve, it&#8217;s important to us to have as clear a sense as possible of who you are, of your intellectual and artistic interests and accomplishments, and of the critical orientation of your research. Your entire application&#8211;transcripts, GRE scores, letters of recommendation, both personal statements, and the critical writing sample&#8211;will be read by the admissions committee and some portions of the application receive particularly close scrutiny. We would like to encourage you to use the Personal Statement and Statement of Purpose on the application to outline where you&#8217;ve been and your orientation to future research. In our effort to assess whether a program like ours is a good &#8220;fit&#8221; for you, it&#8217;s very helpful to have a strong sense of the kind of work you are thinking about, your intellectual and critical style, and overall preparation for Ph.D. study. We are committed to developing a diverse and energetic research community in the program and are eager to recruit students with a range of intellectual, social, and cultural backgrounds, and the diversity of our faculty is an important asset in this regard. Strong applications, then, usually address potential areas of research in the field of performance studies today. Given the depth and range of our faculty, we are interested in students working on both past and present performance traditions, on literary and non-literary forms of performance, and on a range of theoretical and methodological issues ranging across the spectrum of contemporary ethnic, cultural, and performance studies.</p>
<p>There is a great deal of excitement about the program, and about the students who have joined us thus far. Please take the time to carefully read over the graduate program <a href="http://tdps.berkeley.edu/programs-courses/graduate-program/">website</a> and contact Robin Davidson, Graduate Student Affairs Officer, if you have any questions. She can be reached at performancestudies@berkeley.edu or 510-664-7613.  We look forward to hearing from you.</p>
<p>Sincerely,<br />
Shannon Steen<br />
Head Graduate Advisor</p>
<p><strong>PREPARATION AND ADMISSIONS</strong></p>
<p>The Graduate Group admissions committee seeks applicants with qualities that will enable them to succeed in an intensive interdisciplinary program: creativity and analytical skills, practical experience, individual initiative, and intellectual rigor. Priority will be given to applicants whose research interests dovetail well with current faculty resources.</p>
<p>Candidates holding a Bachelor’s degree in theater, literature, performance studies, dance, or any appropriate humanities-related field are eligible to apply for admissions. Candidates with a degree in another field, but with an M.A. in drama or theater arts, or with an M.F.A. in any of the theater arts are also eligible. The Graduate Group is particularly interested in applicants who have already formulated a specific focus of interest, including professional theater practitioners who demonstrate a capacity for and training in advanced scholarly study.</p>
<p>It is vital that you thoroughly read all the graduate program information provided on this website (including the <a href="http://tdps.berkeley.edu/programs-courses/graduate-program/graduate-program-frequently-asked-questions/">FAQs</a>) as well as the information that accompanies the on-line graduate application.</p>
<p><strong>As part of the application, you are required to submit the following:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Personal Statement</li>
<li>Statement of Purpose</li>
<li>Critical Writing Sample &#8211; Follow the &#8220;Performance Studies Program&#8221; link in the application menu to upload this document, 15-20 pages</li>
<li>Resume/CV  &#8211; Follow the &#8220;Supporting Materials&#8221; link in the application menu to upload your CV (include publications/presentations, honors/awards)</li>
<li>Three letters of recommendation</li>
<li>All college transcripts (unofficial copies to be uploaded to the application)</li>
<li>Grades (calculate cumulative undergrad GPA and graduate GPA, if applicable)</li>
<li>GRE scores (&lt;5 years old) &amp; TOEFL scores (if applicable), Berkeley code =4833</li>
<li>Application fee</li>
</ul>
<p><strong><em>IMPORTANT:  All items listed above are</em><em> required by our program and your application will not be considered without them.  However, not every graduate program at UC Berkeley asks for all of this information so some of these items ma</em></strong><em><strong>y not be listed as &#8220;Required&#8221; in the &#8220;Review&#8221; section of the general application and missing items will not limit your ability to select &#8220;Submit.&#8221;  Therefore, it is crucial that you ensure that your application include all of the Performance Studies requirements listed above before submitting it.</strong></em></p>
<p>The Graduate Application for Admission and Fellowships for UC Berkeley is available on-line in early September and is <strong>due December 1,</strong> <strong>8:59 pm (PST), </strong>for consideration for the following academic year. Applicants will hear about the status of their application by late March. To apply, visit <a href="http://grad.berkeley.edu/admissions/index.shtml">http://grad.berkeley.edu/admissions/index.shtml</a></p>
	</div><!-- .entry-content -->
</article><!-- #post-319 -->

<article id="post-292" class="group post-container">
	<header class="entry-header">
		<h1 class="entry-title">Current Graduate Students</h1>
	</header><!-- .entry-header -->

	<div class="entry-content">
		<p><b style="color: #222222;">Juan</b><b style="color: #222222;">&nbsp;M. Aldape:&nbsp;</b><span style="color: #222222;">MA in International Performance Research from the University of Warwick (UK). As practitioner and researcher, his current work focuses on movement, migration and mapping discourses related to undocumented spaces and choreographic processes. Most recently, he co-founded A PerFarmance Project, site-specific collaborations between farmers and performers researching the concept of food security from rural and urban perspectives. He is an Erasmus Mundus Scholar, a regular contributor to loveDancemore performance journal, and the e-resource convener for the International Federation for Theatre Research’s Performance as Research working group. He holds a BFA in Modern Dance and BA in Anthropology from the University of Utah (USA). Email:&nbsp;</span><a style="color: #1155cc;" href="mailto:juanmaldape@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"> juanmaldape@gmail.com</a>&nbsp; Website: <a href="%20          www.juanmaldape.com">www.juanmaldape.com</a></p>
<p><b>Miyuki Baker</b><b>: </b>B.A. Studio Arts, Asian Studies, Swarthmore College (2012). Miyuki is a resident of the place where many circles overlap. They are a queer, multi-racial/lingual artist, activist &amp; academic passionate about using common or discarded objects, stories, zines, and performance in public spaces to make accessible art. Their research examines how we cultivate “hope” and meaning through space, architecture and the environment. Email:&nbsp;<a href="mailto:miyuki.baker@berkeley.edu" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">miyuki.baker@berkeley.edu</a>&nbsp;Website:&nbsp;<a href="http://heymiyuki.wordpress.com/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" data-saferedirecturl="https://www.google.com/url?hl=en&amp;q=http://heymiyuki.wordpress.com&amp;source=gmail&amp;ust=1504123399285000&amp;usg=AFQjCNHwT1PjNc9IttYmv1jXqT2yAc2OVA">heymiyuki.wordpress.com</a></p>
<p><b>Jennifer McPherson Coluccio</b>: B.A. Philosophy, English Literature, University of California, Los Angeles; M.A. Theatre Arts, California State University, Los Angeles. Jennifer is a performer, writer, and scholar with an interest in the intersections of affect, cognition, and the performance of psychopathology. She is concerned with the implications of a poststructural-empirical binary as it relates to the biological, social, and political transmission of affective dis-ease. Email:&nbsp;<a href="mailto:jennifer.coluccio@berkeley.edu">jennifer.coluccio@berkeley.edu</a></p>
<p><b>Miyoko Conley</b><b>: </b>B.F.A, Theatre, New York University; M.A., Individualized Study (Playwriting and Japanese Popular Culture), New York University. Miyoko researches transnational media, fan cultures, and affective technologies, with a focus on Japanese and South Korean popular culture. More broadly, she writes about the intersections of theatre and popular culture, and examines how media phenomenon impact traditional theatre spaces, as well as theatricality in online spaces. Miyoko is also a playwright and performer, and her work engages with what it means to perform with technology.<b> &nbsp;</b>Email:&nbsp;<a href="mailto:miko@berkeley.edu" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">miko@berkeley.edu</a></p>
<p><b>Lashon Daley:&nbsp;</b>B.A. English, University of Miami (2005); M.F.A. Writing, Sarah Lawrence College (2008); M.A. Folklore, University of California, Berkeley (2015).&nbsp; Lashon is a PhD scholar in Performance Studies at the University of California, Berkeley and an emerging storyteller.&nbsp; Her research focuses on the performances of Brer Rabbit tales within contemporary U.S. culture.&nbsp;She is a 2014 Callaloo Poetry Fellow and a 2015 UC Berkeley Chancellor Fellow.&nbsp;Her work has appeared in <i>O, The Oprah Magazine</i>, <i>Storytelling Magazine</i>, and <i>Underwater New York</i>. Her children’s book, <i>Mr. Okra Sells Fresh Fruits and Vegetables</i>, was published by Pelican Publishing in February 2016.&nbsp; Lashon is also the creator of Stories&amp;Slams, a podcast that focuses on everyday stories.&nbsp; More information can be found on her website at <a href="http://www.lashondaley.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">www.lashondaley.com</a>. Email:&nbsp;<a href="mailto:l.daley@berkeley.edu" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">l.daley@berkeley.edu</a></p>
<p><b>Bélgica L. del Río:</b>&nbsp;B.A. in Dance and English, University of California Riverside. Bélgica explores the body’s oscillating meanings and power across ethnicity and culture. She is especially interested in technology’s intersection with the performance of identity and the politics of representation in cinema, theatre and popular dance. Her recent research interests include digital culture, racialization processes, and the global circulation and appropriation of ethnic dance. She is also concerned with the discursive shift digitality brings to theories of embodied knowledge, identity, and performance. Email: <a href="mailto:belgica@berkeley.edu" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">belgica@berkeley.edu</a></p>
<p><strong>Jess Dorrance</strong>&nbsp;is a writer, curator, and PhD student. She writes about the intersections between art, performance, and queer, feminist, and anti-racist politics. She is the co-editor, with Antke Engel, of&nbsp;<em><a href="http://www.queer-institut.de/en/publikation-bossing-images/" data-saferedirecturl="https://www.google.com/url?hl=en&amp;q=http://www.queer-institut.de/en/publikation-bossing-images/&amp;source=gmail&amp;ust=1504716986507000&amp;usg=AFQjCNErdlam6YxWPsUX_kfv4Spk-nq8Xg">Bossing Images: The Power of Images, Queer Art, and Politics</a>&nbsp;</em>(NGBK, 2012), which grew out of an&nbsp;<a href="http://bossingimages-blog.tumblr.com/" data-saferedirecturl="https://www.google.com/url?hl=en&amp;q=http://bossingimages-blog.tumblr.com/&amp;source=gmail&amp;ust=1504716986507000&amp;usg=AFQjCNGGPnKx1vGNRgY8UIacoQ-lrGflwQ">eponymous series of experimental events</a>. She is also a long-time team member of the&nbsp;<a href="http://www.queer-institut.de/en/" data-saferedirecturl="https://www.google.com/url?hl=en&amp;q=http://www.queer-institut.de/en/&amp;source=gmail&amp;ust=1504716986507000&amp;usg=AFQjCNEuK9ueTVRqqCzXNiOvtETqkSVTtQ">Institute for Queer Theory</a>, Berlin. Jess curates short film programs and organizes workshops in Berlin, Montreal, and elsewhere, most recently the workshop “Visibility and Violence in Late-Capitalist Digital Democracy” (QPIRG Concordia, 2015). She holds an MA in Art History, with an emphasis in Gender and Women’s Studies, from McGill University (2014), as well as a BA in Art History and English Literature from McGill University (2008). Email: <a href="mailto:jessica.dorrance@gmail.com">jessica.dorrance@gmail.com</a></p>
<p><b style="color: #222222;">Natalia Duong</b><span style="color: #222222;">&nbsp;is a performance artist, choreographer, and writer, based in the San Francisco Bay Area. Her research interweaves performance studies, disability studies, and critical race theory to examine embodied transmissions of the herbicide Agent Orange across human and non-human bodies in Vietnam and the United States. Natalia is a company member of The Lonely Painter Project and Poetic Theater Productions. She holds a Bachelor&#8217;s degree in Psychology and Dance from Stanford University and a Masters degree in Performance Studies from New York University. She is currently a Ph.D. candidate at University of California, Berkeley in Performance Studies with a designated emphasis in Women, Gender, and Sexuality Studies. Email:&nbsp;</span><a style="color: #1155cc;" href="mailto:natalia.duong@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">natalia.duong@gmail.com</a></p>
<p><strong>Randi Evans</strong>’&nbsp;work and research explores the intersections of dance studies, cultural studies, curatorial practice, and social and community-based practices. She holds a BFA in dance from Cornish College of the Arts, MA in cultural studies from the University of Washington, and certificate in curatorial practice in performance from Wesleyan University. In addition to her academic background she has worked in community-based organizations in arts administration and as a teaching artist. Most recently she has been teaching courses on contemporary performance practices to first year students at the University of Washington Bothell. Email:&nbsp;<a href="mailto:randimariec@gmail.com">randimariec@gmail.com</a></p>
<p><strong>Thea Gold</strong>: B.A. Music and Electrical Engineering, UC-Berkeley; M.A. Interdisciplinary Arts, Tel Aviv University; Graduate work, Near Eastern Studies, UC-Berkeley. Ongoing interests in the fields of religion, queer studies, music, and disability studies.  Email:&nbsp;<a href="mailto:thea@berkeley.edu">thea@berkeley.edu</a></p>
<p><b>Julia Havard</b><b>:&nbsp;</b>B.A. History of Science, minor in Dance, Harvard University. Julia is interested in the embodiment of trauma and the effect of bodily memories on physical movement and gesture. She currently works at a health clinic educating young people in LGBTQ communities about the Affordable Care Act and wants to look more in depth at how barriers to affirming healthcare relate to institutionalized and interpersonal violence. Through her dance practice, she has been exploring reframing of personal and social history.<b>&nbsp;</b>Email:<b>&nbsp;</b><a href="mailto:jhavard@berkeley.edu">jhavard@berkeley.edu</a></p>
<p><b>Martha Herrera-Lasso: </b>MA in Theatre from the University of British Columbia (Vancouver) and a BA in Playwriting from the National University in Mexico City (UNAM). She has worked as a writer and developer for theatre and television in Mexico and Canada, and is currently the co-director of the New Play Reading Series at UC Berkeley. She is concerned with the practical and theoretical implications of bi and tri-national theater collaborations amongst Mexico, Canada and the United States, read through the politics of linguistic, cultural and aesthetic translation. Email:&nbsp;<a href="mailto:herreralassomartha@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">herreralassomartha@gmail.com</a></p>
<p><strong> Megan Hoetger:&nbsp;</strong>PhD candidate in the Department of Theater, Dance, and Performance Studies with Designated Emphases in Critical Theory and Film. Hoetger&#8217;s dissertation,&nbsp;<i>Rude &amp; Playful Shadows: Kurt Kren and the Performances of Cinema, 1964-1989</i>, tracks the development of transnational distribution networks for and communities of underground and experimental time-based art through the Cold War period. Her research has been supported by the&nbsp;German Academic Exchange Service (DAAD), the Getty Research Institute, and the Max Kade Foundation. In addition to her scholarship, Hoetger also works regularly as an organizer of time-based art events and has organized several screenings on the UC Berkeley campus, as well as performance events at artist run spaces across the Los Angeles area. She has worked as the graduate student coordinator for the Berkeley Center for New Media&#8217;s History and Theory of New Media lecture series (2013-15); and has co-organized working groups in contemporary art (2014-16) and sound studies (2015-16) on the UC Berkeley campus. For the 2017-18 academic year Hoetger will be organizing the UC Berkeley Critical Theory Program&#8217;s working group, entitled &#8220;Collaboration, Co-operatives, and Coalition-building.&#8221; Some of her writings on performance, technology, mediatization, and spectatorship have appeared in journal publications including&nbsp;<i>e-misférica</i>,&nbsp;<i>Perform<wbr>ance Research</i>, and&nbsp;<i>X-TRA: Contemporary Art Quarterly</i>. In fall 2017 her writing will also appear in the D.A.P. book&nbsp;<i>Double Issue</i>, which brings together a collection of writings from/on the performance festival that accompanied the Getty Museum&#8217;s landmark 2012&nbsp;Pacific Standard Time initiative. Email:&nbsp;<a href="mailto:mhoetger@berkeley.edu" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">mhoetger@berkeley.edu</a></p>
<p><strong>Paige Johnson</strong>:&nbsp;<span style="color: #000000;">PhD Candidate in Performance Studies with a Designated Emphasis in Gender and Women&#8217;s Studies (UC Berkeley); B.A. Theatre and Cultural Anthropology, Columbia University; Mellon-Mays Fellow; Fulbright Fellow. Paige&#8217;s work sits at the convergence of performance studies, queer studies and Southeast Asian Studies. Currently working in Indonesia, Paige brings a cross-disciplinary intelligence as both a scholar and performer to her work with Male-to-Female trans communities known locally as&nbsp;</span><i style="color: #000000;">Waria</i><span style="color: #000000;">.&nbsp;</span><span style="color: #000000;">Focusing on a large constellation of &nbsp;performative practices, Paige&nbsp;</span><span style="color: #000000;">explores how “Waria”—as an identity, point of identification, social signifier of difference, and node within transnational queer codes—manifests through various “genres” of performance enacted by Waria-identified subjects, seeking to understand Waria as both subject position&nbsp;</span><span style="color: #000000;">and aesthetic demarcation. In addition to her own research Paige has directed a TDPS workshop production of&nbsp;<i>The Maids</i>&nbsp;&nbsp;and currently co-leads the Color of New Media working group with Professor Gail de Kosnik as well as the Queer Theory in South and Southeast Asia working group with Darren Arquero.</span><br />
<a href="mailto:pmj2103@gmail.com">pmj2103@gmail.com</a></p>
<p><strong>Caleb Luna</strong>:&nbsp;B.A., Anthropology and Women’s and Gender Studies, The University of Texas at Austin (2015).&nbsp;Caleb is a working class fat, brown, queer, living, writing and dancing in Oakland, California. Their work explores the intersections of fatness, desire, fetishism, white supremacy and colonialism from a queer of color lens. You can find their writing on Black Girl Dangerous, Everyday Feminism and The Body Is Not An Apology.&nbsp;<a href="mailto:ctluna@berkeley.edu" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">ctluna@berkeley.edu</a></p>
<p><b style="color: #222222;">Christian Nagler</b><span style="color: #222222;">&nbsp;is a performer, writer and translator. He has performed with Anna Halprin, Isak Immanuel, Yuko Kaseki and Open Experiments Ensemble. His work has recently been presented at the Berkeley Art Museum, Headlands Center for the Arts, Southern Exposure, and the Kadist Foundation. His novel&nbsp;</span><i style="color: #222222;">The Capitalist,&nbsp;</i><span style="color: #222222;">is forthcoming in 2014. His writing can recently be found in&nbsp;</span><i style="color: #222222;">Fillip</i><span style="color: #222222;">,&nbsp;</span><i style="color: #222222;">Six Lines of Flight</i><span style="color: #222222;">&nbsp;(UC Press),&nbsp;</span><i style="color: #222222;">Somatic Engagement</i><span style="color: #222222;">&nbsp;(Chainlinks Books)&nbsp;</span><i style="color: #222222;">Encyclopedia</i><span style="color: #222222;">,&nbsp;</span><i style="color: #222222;">Aufgabe,&nbsp;</i><span style="color: #222222;">and&nbsp;</span><i style="color: #222222;">Performance Research</i><span style="color: #222222;">. He has translated works by the political economist Alberto Masferrer, as well as writings by the contemporary novelist Horacio Castellanos Moya and psychoanalytic theorist Heriberto Yépez. He currently teaches writing and new genres at the San Francisco Art Institute. Email: &nbsp;</span><a style="color: #1155cc;" href="mailto:christiannagler@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">christiannagler@gmail.com</a></p>
<p><b>Aparna Nambiar:&nbsp;</b>BSc. Life Sciences, National University of Singapore; M.A. Theatre Studies, University of Amsterdam<b>;&nbsp;</b>M.A. International Performance Research, University of Warwick. Aparna is an Indian classical dancer and performance studies scholar based in Singapore. Her research thus far has examined the genesis and evolution of minority Indian performance practices in Singapore, and the ongoing negotiations of Singaporean identity that manifest performatively and corporeally. Her interests include diaspora studies, traditional performance practices in contemporary Asia and the interventions of global capital flows on Asian culture. Email:&nbsp;<a href="mailto:aparna.r.nambiar@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">aparna.r.nambiar@gmail.com</a></p>
<p><strong>Lyndsey Ogle:</strong>&nbsp;B.F.A. Acting, Northern Illinois University; M.A. Individualized Studies (Interdisciplinary Curation and Digital Culture), New York University.&nbsp;&nbsp;Lyndsey is an interdisciplinary artist and curator exploring the intersections of cultural discourse, narrative and technology through performance, public engagement and online content. Her current research interests include socially engaged practice, social networks as performance, interdisciplinary discourse and identity-making within digital culture. Email:&nbsp;<a href="mailto:lyndseyogle@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">lyndseyogle@gmail.com</a></p>
<p><strong><b>Toshi Pau</b>:</strong>&nbsp;B.A. Asian &amp; Middle Eastern Studies, the College of William and Mary &nbsp;(2014); M.A. East Asian Studies, Duke University (2015). Scholar, actor, and dancer. Toshi’s critical research interests lie in analyses of race, gender, and queer theory in performance. His current projects focus on histories of sex, Asian and Asian-American sexual cultures and communities, sexual labor, and the education of sex. Through this work, Toshi hopes to destigmatize discussions of sex as social taboo and reimagine possibilities of sex as performative modes of liberation, freedom, and empowerment. Email:&nbsp;<a href="mailto:toshi.pau@berkeley.edu">toshi.pau@berkeley.edu</a></p>
<p><strong>Kimberly Richards</strong> is a recipient of the Social Sciences and Humanities Research Council of Canada Graduate Scholarship, the Edward Hildebrand&nbsp;Graduate Fellowship in Canadian Studies, and the Heather&nbsp;McCallum Award from the Canadian Association of Theatre Research.&nbsp;Her dissertation,&nbsp;“Crude Stages of the Anthropocene: Performance and Petro-Imperialism” examines oil frontiers as material and representational spaces constituted through practice, representation and acts of the imagination. She considers how performance practices, such as spectacles and festivals, socially construct and performatively produce oil frontiers, and how theatrical tactics at petro-protests work to resist the expansion of petro-imperialism. Her research interests include performance theory, petrocriticism, the energy and environmental humanities, postcolonial ecocriticism, and human rights. She holds a B.A. and M.A.&nbsp;in English from the University of Calgary. Email:&nbsp;<a href="mailto:krichar@berkeley.edu" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">krichar@berkeley.edu</a></p>
<div>
<div>
<div>
<p><b>JT (Jennif(f)er Tamayo)</b>: BA Human Development, Fundamentals: Issues &amp; Texts, University of Chicago (2005), MFA Creative Writing-Poetry, Louisiana State University (2010). Born in Bogotá, Jennif(f)er is Nancy’s daughter. She is a queer, latinx writer and performer whose research attends to (the performativity of) contemporary poetry readings, asking the questions: what knowledges does the voice hold that are distinct from language; if a body is a site of ancestral knowledges, how do the violent legacies of slavery and settler colonialism haunt contemporary poetry “readings”? &nbsp;A former CantoMundo Fellow and Hemispheric Institute of Performance and Politics Emerge Fellow, Jenni(f)fer’s books include [Red Missed Aches] (Switchback, 2011), Poems are the Only Real Bodies (Bloof Books 2013) and YOU DA ONE (2014/15 reprint Noemi Books &amp; Letras Latinas) and her writing has been published in Poetry magazine, Best American Experimental Poetry, Mandorla: Writing from the Americas, and &nbsp;Angels of the Americlypse; An Anthology of New Latin@ Writing<strong>. </strong>Email:<strong>&nbsp;</strong><a href="mailto:j_tamayo@berkeley.edu"> j_tamayo@berkeley.edu</a></p>
<p><strong>Tonika Sealy Thompson</strong> is a PhD student in Performance Studies who is concerned with Caribbean cultural and political thought, multilingual/hemispheric Black diaspora studies, Gender Womens and Sexuality studies and Afro Asian connections She grew up in Barbados and has been living and working globally as a curator, festival director and cultural consultant on projects in the Caribbean, Europe, Africa, and the Asia Pacific regions. She has served as artistic coordinator of the Africa Caribbean and Pacific Arts Festival, and is the founder of the Fish and Dragon Festival a platform for creative exchange between the Caribbean and China. Email:&nbsp;<a href="mailto:tonika_sealythompson@berkeley.edu">tonika_sealythompson@berkeley.edu</a></p>
</div>

<article id="post-511" class="group post-container">
	<header class="entry-header">
		<h1 class="entry-title">Ph.D. Alumni</h1>
	</header><!-- .entry-header -->

	<div class="entry-content">
		<h2><strong>Completed Ph.D. Degrees in Performance Studies</strong></h2>
<p><em>Since inception of the program in 1998</em></p>
<p>Graduates from the PhD in Performance Studies are hired in a great range of disciplines, from art history and literature to theatre, communications and Asian American studies.</p>
<p><strong>Anderson, Patrick</strong><br />
“So Much Wasted’: Violence Performed In Anorexia Nervosa, Staged Fasts, and Hunger Striking” SP05<br />
UC San Diego, Associate Professor, Communications, Director of Critical Gender Studies</p>
<p><strong>Bayraktar, Nilgun</strong><br />
“Moving Images Against the Current: The Aesthetics and Geopolitics of (Im)mobility in Contemporary Europe” FL11<br />
2011 UC Berkeley, R&amp;C Lectureship<br />
2012 Bogazici University in Istanbul, Turkey, Instructor, Humanities<br />
2015 California College of the Arts, Assistant Professor, Visual Studies</p>
<p><b>Baron, Michelle</b><br />
“Queering US Public Mourning Rituals: Funerals, Performance, and the Construction of Normativity” SU11<br />
2011 Oberlin College,Visiting Assistant Professor<br />
2012 Hobart and William Smith Colleges, Assistant Professor, Women’s Studies</p>
<p><strong>Belmar, Sima</strong><br />
&#8220;Easier Said Than Done: Talking Identity in Late Twentieth-Century American Concert Dance: S15<br />
2015 UC Berkeley, Lecturer, Department of Theater, Dance, and Performance Studies</p>
<p><strong>Boucai, Marc</strong><br />
“Narrating Normal: Arabs, Queers, Neoliberal Spectatorship” FL13<br />
2014 Theatre Coordinator at AS220, Providence, RI</p>
<p><strong>Boyle, (Michael) Shane</strong><br />
“The Ambivalence of Resistance: West German Antiauthoritarian Performance after the Age of Affluence” FL12<br />
Spring 2013 &#8211; Harvard University, Lecturer, College Writing Program<br />
2013 Stanford University, Postdoctoral Lecturer in the Immersion in the Arts: Living in Culture Program<br />
2014 Queen Mary, University of London, School of English and Drama, Lecturer in Drama, Theatre, and Performance Studies, Director of MA in Theatre and Performance</p>
<p><strong>Brain, Naomi</strong><br />
&#8220;Black Power of Hip Hop Dance: On Kinesthetic Politics&#8221; S15<br />
2015 (On leave 2015-16) University of Washington, Bothell, Assistant Professor, Performance Studies<br />
2015-2016 UC President&#8217;s Postdoctoral Fellowship, UC Riverside</p>
<p><strong>Burriss, Catherine</strong><br />
“Performing Theory: Gendered and Erotic Complications in Cinquecento Italian Comedies, and some English Reverberations” FL06<br />
CSU Channel Islands, Associate Professor, Performing Arts</p>
<p><strong>Cappelli, Renu</strong><br />
“Inadmissible Presence: Objecthood, Spectacle, and the Theatricality of Race” FL07<br />
2008-2011 Stanford University, Post-doctoral Scholar, Introduction to the Humanities<br />
2013 UC San Diego, Lecturer, Critical Gender Studies</p>
<p><strong>Case, Gretchen</strong><br />
“Medical Scarring and the Performance of Memory” FL05<br />
Duke University, University Writing Program Fellow<br />
Northwestern University, Adjunct Lecturer, Medical Humanities and Bioethics Program<br />
2011 University of Utah School of Medicine, Assistant Professor, Division of Medical Ethics and Humanities</p>
<p><strong>Casey, Carrie Gaiser</strong><br />
“Ballet’s Feminisms: Genealogy and Gender in Twentieth-Century American Ballet History” FL09<br />
St. Mary’s College of California, Adjunct Professor, Liberal Education for Arts Professionals program</p>
<p><strong>Crow, Heather</strong><br />
“POSSESSIONS: Animated Bodies in Mediated Performance” FL06<br />
Texas Tech University, Assistant Professor of Interdisciplinary Arts, Fine Arts Doctoral Program</p>
<p><strong>Davis, Reid</strong><br />
“Sissy Warriors: Perversity, Performance, and the Unruly Child” FL06<br />
St. Mary’s College, Adjunct Professor, Ethnic Studies and Performing Arts</p>
<p><strong>Duffly, Catherine</strong><br />
“From Farm to Table to Stage: Performing Food Politics” FL11<br />
2011 UC Berkeley, R&amp;C Lecturer and California College of the Arts, Lecturer<br />
2012 Reed College, Assistant Professor, Department of Theatre</p>
<p><strong>Ferro-Murray, Ashley</strong><br />
&#8220;Choreography in the Digital Era: Dancing the Cultural Differences of Technology&#8221; SP16<br />
2016 Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute, NY, Curator of Theater and Dance at the Experimental Media and Performing Arts Center (EMPAC)</p>
<p><strong>Fisek, Emine</strong><br />
“Incorporating Immigrants: Theatrical Aid Work and the Politics of Witnessing in France” SP10<br />
Johns Hopkins University, Mellon Postdoctoral Fellowship in the Humanities, Krieger School of Arts and Science, German and Romance Languages and Literatures<br />
2012 Bogazici University, Turkey, Associate Professor, Department of Western Languages and Literature</p>
<p><strong>Fisher, Margaret</strong><br />
“Recovery of Ezra Pound’s Third Opera Collis O Heliconii: The Transmission of History Through Song” SP03<br />
Second Evening Arts Publishing</p>
<p><strong>Gough, Kathleen</strong><br />
“Bleeding Regions: Performance and Politics in the ‘Backwaters’ of the Atlantic” FL05<br />
University of Glasgow, Lecturer, Department of Theatre, Film and Television Studies and Advisor of Studies, Arts College Academic and Student Administration<br />
2014 University of Vermont, <span style="color: #141823;">Assistant Professor and Resident Dramaturge,Theatre Department </span></p>
<p><strong>Hagstrom Stahl, Kristina</strong><br />
“Melancholy Traces: Performing the Work of Mourning” FL06<br />
Postdoctoral Fellow in the Humanities at Lund University, Sweden and also teaches at the Stockholm Academy of Dramatic Arts</p>
<p><strong>Hoffmann, Beth</strong><br />
“Acting without Guarantees: The Politics of Form in Contemporary British Performance” FL08<br />
George Mason University, Assistant Professor, English Department</p>
<p><strong>Johung, Jennifer</strong><br />
“Replacements: From the Primordial Hut to the Digital Network” SP08<br />
University of Wisconsin, Milwaukee, Associate Professor, Department of Art History</p>
<p><strong>Kokontis, Kate</strong><br />
“Performative Returns and the Rememory of History: genealogy and performativity in the American racial state” FL11<br />
2011 New Orleans Center for Creative Arts, Academic Studio: Founding Faculty and Assistant Department Chair, Social Studies</p>
<p><strong>Levin, Laura</strong><br />
“Performing World” SP05<br />
York University, Associate Professor, Theatre Studies and Graduate Program in Communication and Culture</p>
<p><strong>Lu, Joyce</strong><br />
“Dreaming in Other Languages: On the Performance of Autobiographical Narrative as Decolonizing Pedagogy&#8221; SP07<br />
Pomona College, Mellon Postdoctoral Fellow<br />
Claremont Colleges, Assistant Professor, Theatre and Dance</p>
<p><strong>Marshall, Caitlin</strong><br />
&#8220;Power in the Tongue&#8217;: Staging American Voice&#8221; SS16<br />
2016-17 Postdoctoral position in Theater and Performance Studies at the University of Maryland</p>
<p><strong>Mattingly, Kate</strong><br />
&#8220;Set in Motion: Dance Criticism and the Choreographic Apparatus &#8221; S17<br />
2017 University of Utah, School of Dance, Assistant Professor</p>
<p><strong>McGonigal, Jane</strong><br />
“This Might be a Game: Ubiquitous Play Performance at the Turn of the Twenty-First Century” FL06<br />
Institute for the Future, Palo Alto, CA, Director of Games Research and Development</p>
<p><strong>McIvor, Charlotte</strong><br />
“The New Interculturalism: Race, Gender and Immigration in Post-Celtic Tiger Ireland” SP11<br />
National University of Ireland, Galway, Lecturer, Department of English, Director of Postgraduate Studies in Drama</p>
<p><strong>Nguyen, Khai Thu </strong><br />
“Sensing Vietnam: Melodramas of Nation from Colonialism to Market Reform” SP10<br />
University of California, Berkeley, James R. Gray R&amp;C Lecturer, College of Letters and Science<br />
University of California, Berkeley, UC Extension, Special Assistant to the Dean<br />
2016 University of California, Berkeley, Associate Director, Consortium for Interdisciplinary Research</p>
<p><strong>Palacios, Joy Crosby</strong><br />
“Preaching for the Eyes: Priests, Actors, and Ceremonial Splendor in Early Modern France” SU12<br />
2014 Simon Fraser University, Burnaby, BC, Canada, Assistant Professor of Literature, Department of French</p>
<p><strong>Prieur, Nina Billone</strong><br />
“In the System: Art, Prison, and the Performance of Social Welfare” FL10<br />
Duke University, Assistant Professor, Theatre Studies<br />
Georgetown University, Visiting Assistant Professor, Department of Performing Arts</p>
<p><strong>Rafferty, Kelly Ann</strong><br />
“Performing ARTs: Technologies of Participation and Reproduction from Body Art to Bio Art” SP10<br />
Arizona State University, Assistant Professor of Performance Studies<br />
2013: Independent artist, educator, and facilitator in Oakland, San Francisco, and Los Angeles</p>
<p><strong>Ramos, Ivan</strong><br />
&#8220;Sonic Negations: Sound, Affect, and Unbelonging Between Mexico and the United States&#8221; S15<br />
2015-2017 UC President&#8217;s Postdoctoral Fellowship, UC Riverside</p>
<p><strong>Rastovac, Heather</strong><br />
&#8220;Performing (Trans)National Iranianness: The Choreographic Cartographies of Diasporic Iranian Dancers and Performance Artists&#8221; SS16<br />
2016-2017 Mellon Postdoctoral Fellow, Stanford University, Dance</p>
<p><strong>Ricks, Omar</strong><br />
&#8220;On Jubilee: The Performance of Black Leadership in the Afterlife of Slavery&#8221; SP14</p>
<p><strong>Rivera, Takeo</strong><br />
“Minority Models: Masochism, Masculinity, and the Machine in Asian American Cultural Politics&#8221; SP17<br />
2017 Boston University, Department of English, Assistant Professor</p>
<p><strong>Scott, Ariel Osterweis</strong><br />
“Body Impossible: Dynamics of Race, Sexuality, and Virtuosity in the Dance of Desmond Richardson” FL11<br />
Wayne State University Michigan, Assistant Professor of Dance<br />
2014 Skidmore College, Dance Department, Visiting Scholar/Artist<br />
2016 California Institute of the Arts, Assistant Professor, School of Dance</p>
<p><strong>Seetoo, Chia-Yi</strong><br />
“The Political Kinesthetics of Contemporary Dance: Taiwan in Transnational Perspective&#8221; Sp13<br />
Postdoctoral Fellowship at the Shanghai Theatre Academy</p>
<p><strong>Shalson, Lara</strong><br />
“Endurance: Arts, Politics, and Performance” FL08<br />
King&#8217;s College London, Lecturer, Theatre and Performance Studies</p>
<p><strong>Shankar, Karin</strong><br />
&#8220;Molecular Aesthetics: Contemporary Art and Performance in Delhi &#8221; SS16<br />
2016-17  Andrew W. Mellon Global Postdoctoral Fellow at Creative Time in NYC</p>
<p><strong>Sherman, Stephanie</strong><br />
&#8220;(Dis)Plazas and (Dis)Placed Danzas: Space, Trauma, and Moving Bodies in Mexico City&#8221; F16<br />
2017 Visiting Professor, Arts Department, Universidad de las Américas in Puebla, Mexico</p>
<p><strong>Sizemore-Barber, April</strong><br />
“Prismatic Performances: Queer South African Identity and the Deconstruction of the Rainbow Nation” FL13<br />
2014 Hobart and William Smith Colleges, Visiting Assistant Professor, Women&#8217;s Studies<br />
2015 Postdoctoral Scholar Royal Holloway, University<br />
2015-2018 Georgetown, Visiting Assistant Professor, Gender and Sexuality Studies</p>
<p><strong>Stufft, Monica</strong><br />
“Chorus Girl Collective: Early 20<sup>th</sup> Century American Performance Communities and Urban Networking” SP08<br />
University of San Diego, Assistant Professor, Theatre Arts</p>
<p><strong>Taylor, Joanne Stoddard </strong><br />
“21st Century Zombies: New Media, Cinema, and Performance” FL11<br />
Berkeley City College, Adjunct Faculty, Humanities<br />
Diablo Valley College, Adjunct Faculty, Humanities<br />
San Francisco State University, Adjunct Professor, Business</p>
<p><strong>Wallin, Scott</strong><br />
&#8220;Madness in the Making: Psychosocial Disability and Theater&#8221; SP14<br />
2014-15 UC Berkeley, Lecturer, Department of Theater, Dance, and Performance Studies<br />
2015 Stanford University, Postdoctoral Lecturer in the Immersion in the Arts: Living in Culture Program<br />
2016 UC Berkeley, Lecturer, Department of Theater, Dance, and Performance Studies</p>
<p><strong>Williams, Joshua</strong><br />
“Don’t Show A Hyena How Well You Can Bite: Performance, Race and the Animal Subaltern in Eastern Africa&#8221; SP17<br />
2016 Harvard College, Writing Program</p>
<p><strong>Woolf, Brandon</strong><br />
“Paradigmatic Stages: Performing Arts Policy in Post-Wall Berlin” SU14<br />
2016 New York University, Visiting Assistant Professor, English Department</p>
<p><strong>Yapp, Hentyle</strong><br />
&#8220;Minor China: Affect, Performance, &amp; Contemporary China in the Global&#8221; SP14<br />
2014-15 Pomona College, Postdoctoral Appointment<br />
2015 Pomona College, Assistant Professor<br />
2016 New York University, Assistant Professor, Art and Public Policy</p>

<article id="post-327" class="group post-container">
	<header class="entry-header">
		<h1 class="entry-title">Graduate Student Employment</h1>
	</header><!-- .entry-header -->

	<div class="entry-content">
		<p>DEPARTMENT OF THEATER, DANCE, AND PERFORMANCE STUDIES</p>
<p>GSI APPOINTMENT INFORMATION</p>
<p>In the coming academic year, the Department of Theater, Dance, and Performance Studies hopes to make the following appointments. This projection is not a guarantee of the number of ASE positions that will be available or filled.</p>
<p>The Department of Theater, Dance, and Performance Studies abides by University non-discrimination in employment regulations. Within the limits imposed by law or University regulations, the University shall not discriminate against or harass any ASE on the basis of race, color, religion, marital status, national origin, ancestry, sex, sexual orientation, physical or mental disability, medical condition, HIV status, status as a covered veteran, age, citizenship, political affiliation and union activity.</p>
<p>IMPORTANT</p>
<p>Our GSI appointments are generally filled by Performance Studies PhD students.  We do not have openings for students from other campus departments.  For Summer GSI appointments, priority is given first to 4th year Performance Studies PhD Candidates, then to 5th year students.</p>
<p>Our ability to fund all of our students depends on the students’ commitments to the department and to our program.  By accepting the offer of funding and responding to our request for teaching preferences, you become an important part of how we educate our undergraduate students. We will provide you with training, support, and supervision to fulfill this important role and prepare for future careers.  At the same time, you are expected to participate fully in this reciprocal agreement, communicate proactively about your circumstances, and fulfill your teaching commitments.</p>
<p>For more information about GSI appointments, please reference <a href="http://grad.berkeley.edu/financial/graduate-student-employment/">http://grad.berkeley.edu/financial/graduate-student-employment/</a>.</p>
<p>To be considered for any of the GSI positions listed below or others that may become available, Performance Studies students must respond to the Department Chair&#8217;s request for applications and complete the on-line form each year with information about teaching preferences, past experience, and pedagogy classes.   All GSIs must successfully complete the pedagogy class College Writing 375 prior to the first semester as a GSI.</p>
<p>GSI APPOINTMENTS</p>
<p>1.Theater 1A-1B. Performance: Writing and Research.   Three hours of class meeting per week. GSI designs syllabus for a course in reading and composition in connection with the study of dramatic literature; course sections are supervised by faculty coordinator. Course fulfills undergraduate reading and composition requirement. Duties include meeting all class meetings, designing and executing syllabus, assigning and grading writing assignments, quizzes, and exams.</p>
<p>2.Theater 25AC. The Drama of American Cultures: An Introduction to Our Theater.  Three hours of class lecture per week plus discussion sections. GSI attends lectures and teaches two additional discussion sections (1 hour each). Course addresses issues of cultural identity through the study of diverse traditions of American theater. Duties include attending lecture, meeting section meetings, executing syllabus, assigning and grading writing assignments, quizzes, and exams.</p>
<p>3.Theater 26. Introduction to Performance Studies.  Three hours of class meeting per week plus discussion sections. GSI attends lectures and teaches two additional discussion sections (1 hour each). Course raises issues of broad relevance to the fields of theater, dance, and performance studies. Applicants are expected to have a basic grounding in Western and non-Western theater and dance as well as a familiarity with different disciplinary traditions in performance theory. Duties include adapting basic syllabus; executing syllabus; developing, assigning and grading writing assignments, quizzes, and exams.</p>
<p>4.Theater 52AC.  Dance in American Culture.  Three hours of class lecture per week plus discussion sections. GSI attends lectures and teaches two additional discussion sections (1 hour each). Course addresses issues of cultural identity through the study of diverse traditions of American dance. Duties include attending lecture, meeting section meetings, executing syllabus, assigning and grading writing assignments, quizzes, and exams.</p>
<p>5.Dance technique classes – Theater 40, 141, 142, 143. Experienced graduate students who have completed the pedagogy class Theater 340, and whose skills are appropriate to our curricular needs, may occasionally be considered for teaching positions within our dance program.</p>
	</div><!-- .entry-content -->
</article><!-- #post-327 -->

<article id="post-520" class="group post-container">
	<header class="entry-header">
		<h1 class="entry-title">Graduate Group Faculty</h1>
	</header><!-- .entry-header -->

	<div class="entry-content">
		<p>The Graduate Group in Performance Studies is responsible for the Ph.D. program and is comprised of faculty with appointments in the Department of Theater, Dance, and Performance Studies as well as faculty from a range of departments and disciplines with scholarly and teaching interests in the field.</p>
<h3><strong>CORE FACULTY</strong>:</h3>
<p><a href="/people/faculty/brandi-wilkins-catanese/"><em><strong>Brandi Wilkins Catanese</strong></em></a>, Associate Professor, Departments of African American Studies and Theater, Dance, and Performance Studies; Ph.D. Stanford University; African-American Drama and Theater.</p>
<p><a href="/people/faculty/abigail-de-kosnik/"><em><strong>Abigail De Kosnik</strong></em></a>, Associate Professor, Berkeley Center for New Media and Department of Theater, Dance, and Performance Studies; Ph.D. Northwestern University; Technology and Performance; Artistic Appropriation and Remix; Ethnicity, Gender, and Digital Culture; Cultural Studies; Subcultures and Fan Cultures; Marxism and Post-Structuralism.</p>
<p><a href="/people/faculty/sansan-kwan/"><em><strong>SanSan Kwan</strong></em></a>, Associate Professor, Department of Theater, Dance, and Performance Studies: Ph.D. New York University; Critical Dance Studies; Transnational Asian American Studies; Cultural Geography; Theories of Space and Kinesthesia, Interculturalism, Modern Dance, Ballet, and Yoga.</p>
<p><a href="/people/faculty/julia-fawcett/"><em><strong>Julia Fawcett</strong></em></a>, Assistant Professor, Department of Theater, Dance, and Performance Studies; Ph.D. Yale University; Restoration and 18th Century Theater and Performance, Performance Historiography, Intersections Between Literature and Performance, Autobiographical Performance, Urban Space, Celebrity, Gender, and Disability Studies.</p>
<p><a href="/people/faculty/peter-glazer/"><em><strong>Peter Glazer</strong></em></a>, Associate Professor, Department of Theater, Dance, and Performance Studies; Ph.D. Northwestern University; Directing; Adaptation; Performance Theory; 20th century American Theater; Commemorative Performance.</p>
<p><a href="/people/faculty/mark-griffith/"><em><strong>Mark Griffith</strong></em></a>, Professor, Departments of Classics and Theater, Dance, and Performance Studies; Ph.D. Cambridge University; Classical drama and performance; Greek and Latin literature.</p>
<p><a href="/people/faculty/shannon-jackson/"><em><strong>Shannon Jackson</strong></em></a>, Professor, Departments of Rhetoric and Theater, Dance, and Performance Studies; Ph.D. Northwestern University; Performance Studies; Contemporary theater; American cultural history and Performance Historiography; Adaptation.</p>
<p><a href="/people/faculty/angela-marino/"><em><strong>Angela Marino</strong></em></a>,  Assistant Professor, Department of Theater, Dance, and Performance Studies; Ph.D., New York University; politics and performance in the Americas; Latin/o American performance and dramatic literature; popular fiesta and carnival theory.</p>
<p><a href="http://womensstudies.berkeley.edu/about/faculty/trinh-t-minh-ha/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><em><strong>Trinh Minh-ha</strong></em></a>, Professor, Department of Gender and Women&#8217;s Studies; Feminist Theory; Film Theory and production; Comparative Literary and Art Theory; Cultural Politics; Third World Arts and Politics.</p>
<p><a href="http://ethnicstudies.berkeley.edu/people/faculty-profile/laura-perez-1"><em><strong>Laura E. Pérez</strong></em></a>, Associate Professor, Department of Ethnic Studies; Ph.D. Harvard University; Post-1965 U.S. Latina/o Visual, Performance, and Literary Arts; Feminist, &#8220;Minority,&#8221; Post-Colonial, and Cultural Studies theories.</p>
<p><a href="http://womensstudies.berkeley.edu/about/faculty/juana-maria-rodriguez/"><strong><em>Juana Maria Rodriguez</em></strong></a>, Professor, Department of Ethnic Studies; Ph.D. UC Berkeley; Queer Theory and Cultural Activism; Latin@ Popular Cultures; Performance Studies; Critical Race Theory; Sex and Sexuality Studies; Technology and Media Arts.</p>
<p><a href="http://complit.berkeley.edu/people/miryam-sas/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><em><strong>Miryam Sas</strong></em></a>, Professor, Departments of Comparative Literature and Film Studies; Ph.D. Yale University; 20th century poetry; Japanese Experimental Theater and Dance; Memory and Trauma; Mass Media and Cultural Studies; Film.</p>
<p><a href="http://music.berkeley.edu/people/mary-ann-smart/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><em><strong>Mary Ann Smart</strong></em></a>, Professor, Department of Music; Ph.D. Cornell University; opera;  music and gender; music and politics; historical acting and staging; live performance and technology in contemporary opera.</p>
<p><a href="/people/faculty/shannon-steen/"><em><strong>Shannon Steen</strong></em></a>, Associate Professor, Department of Theater, Dance, and Performance Studies; Ph.D. Stanford University; performance and critical race studies (especially the intersection of African and Asian American histories), American Studies, globalization and American urban development, and post/modernisms.</p>
<p><em><strong><a href="http://ealc.berkeley.edu/people/volpp-sophie" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Sophie Volpp</a></strong></em>, Associate Professor, Departments of Comparative Literature and East Asian Languages and Cultures; Ph.D. Harvard University; classical Chinese performance, Chinese literature of the seventeenth through nineteenth centuries, history of performance, gender theory, the history of sexuality, and the representation of material culture.</p>
<p><a href="http://anthropology.berkeley.edu/users/alexei-yurchak" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><em><strong>Alexei Yurchak</strong></em></a>, Associate Professor, Department of Anthropology; Ph.D. Duke University; theories of discourse, power and performance, the politics of aesthetics, irony and ideology, contemporary media, Russian informal art, Soviet state socialism and postsocialism, cities and urban space.</p>
<h3><strong>AFFILIATED FACULTY:</strong></h3>
<p><a href="http://womensstudies.berkeley.edu/about/department-faculty/paola-bacchetta/"><strong><em>Paola Bacchetta</em></strong></a>, Associate Professor, Department of Gender and Women&#8217;s Studies; Ph.D. in Sociology from The Sorbonne, Paris; transnational feminist and queer theories; inseparabilities of gender, sexuality, &#8220;race&#8221;-racism, postcoloniality; Hindu nationalism; global political conflict; feminist and queer of color, and right wing movement discourses and practices in the U.S., India  and France; transnational feminist and queer alliances.</p>
<p><a href="http://anthropology.berkeley.edu/users/charles-l-briggs" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><em><strong>Charles Briggs</strong></em></a>, Alan Dundes Distinguished Professor in Folklore, Department of Anthropology; Ph.D. University of Chicago; performing the diseased body and its therapeutic intervention, biomedical and vernacular; theorizing relations between narrative and violence; mediatization and its reified objects; creating modern subjects by creating their &#8220;traditional&#8221; Others.</p>
<p><a href="http://complit.berkeley.edu/people/judith-butler/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><em><strong>Judith Butler</strong></em></a>, Professor, Department of Comparative Literature and Program of Critical Theory; Ph.D. Yale University; performance and identity; gender and sexual politics; human rights; anti-war politics; messianic gestures in Kafka and Benjamin; philosophical fictions in Freud’s work; gender in translation.</p>
<p><a href="/people/faculty/joe-goode/"><em><strong>Joe Goode</strong></em></a>, Professor, Department of Theater, Dance, and Performance Studies; BFA, Virginia Commonwealth University; choreography and interdisciplinary performance.</p>
<p><a href="http://music.berkeley.edu/people/jocelyne-guilbault/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><em><strong>Jocelyne Guilbault</strong></em></a>, Professor, Department of Music; Ph.D. University of Michigan; Ethnomusicology; Caribbean Musics (popular and traditional); Creolization; Power; Cultural Politics; Nationalism; Diaspora.</p>
<p><a href="http://ieas.berkeley.edu/faculty/jones.html"><strong><em>Andrew Jones</em></strong></a>, Professor, Department of East Asian Languages &amp; Cultures; Ph.D. UC Berkeley; Children&#8217;s Literature; Chinese Popular Music; East Asian Languages and Cultures; Literary Translation; Media Technology; Modern Chinese Fiction; Sonic Culture.</p>
<p><a href="http://german.berkeley.edu/author/tkaes/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><em><strong>Anton Kaes</strong></em></a>, Professor, Departments of German and Film Studies; Ph.D. Stanford University; modern German theater (Expressionism, Brecht; and the theater of the 1920s); postmodernist theater and film; the relationship between theater and film; theory of film, Critical Theory, and Cultural Studies.</p>
<p><a href="http://sociology.berkeley.edu/faculty/john-lie" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><em><strong>John Lie</strong></em></a>, Professor, Department of Sociology and Center for Korean Studies; Ph.D. Harvard University; social theory, political economy, Korean diaspora.</p>
<p><a href="http://anthropology.berkeley.edu/users/saba-mahmood" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><em><strong>Saba Mahmood</strong></em></a>, Associate Professor, Department of Anthropology; Ph.D. Stanford University; Anthropology of Subject Formation, Liberalism, and Secular Modernity; Feminist and Poststructuralist Theory; Religion and Politics; Islam, the Middle East, and South Asia.</p>
<p><a href="http://english.berkeley.edu/profiles/68" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><em><strong>Susan Schweik</strong></em></a>, Professor, Department of English; Ph.D. Yale University; Disability Studies; Poetry; 20th-Century American Literature; 19th-Century American literature; Cultural Studies; Gender &amp; Sexuality Studies; Race and Ethnicity.</p>
<p><strong>RETIRED FACULTY</strong>:</p>
<p><a href="http://sseas.berkeley.edu/people/faculty/vasudha-dalmia" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><em><strong>Vasudha Dalmia</strong></em></a>, Professor, Department of South and South East Asian Studies; Ph.D. Jawaharlal Nehru University; Hindi Drama and other Indian Theater traditions; Brecht.</p>
<p><a href="http://vcresearch.berkeley.edu/dru-dougherty" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><em><strong>Dru Dougherty</strong></em></a>, Professor, Department of Spanish and Portuguese; Ph.D. Harvard University; Spanish drama, especially of the early 20th century.</p>
<p><a href="/people/faculty/mel-gordon/"><em><strong>Mel Gordon</strong></em></a>, Professor, Department of Theater, Dance, and Performance Studies; Ph.D. New York University; Modern and Contemporary European Theater; Popular entertainment.</p>
<p><a href="http://fm.berkeley.edu/people/faculty/linda-williams/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"><em><strong>Linda Williams</strong></em></a>, Professor, Departments of Film Studies and Rhetoric; Ph.D. University of Colorado; Popular Moving-Image Genres (Pornography, Melodrama, and &#8220;Body Genres&#8221; of all sorts); Eastern and Western Forms of Melodrama; Film Theory.</p>
<h3></h3>
<p><em>Core Faculty: </em><br />
<em> Core Faculty may serve as Chair, Co-Chair, or Additional Member on student committees but not as Academic Senate Representative. In addition, they may serve periodically on the Executive Committee (which sets policy, conducts admissions, and reviews student progress). Core Faculty regularly attend Performance Studies program events&#8211;the welcoming reception, Performance Practicum performances, the 5th year lectures. They constitute the voting faculty of the Group, and are recommended to the Graduate Dean for appointment to the Graduate Group in Performance Studies.</em></p>
<p><em>Affiliated Faculty: </em><br />
<em>Affiliated Faculty may serve on student committees as the Academic Senate Representative or as an Additional Member, but may not chair a committee. They are invited to all Graduate Group events.</em></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
	</div><!-- .entry-content -->

<article id="post-560" class="group post-container">
	<header class="entry-header">
		<h1 class="entry-title">Graduate Program FAQs</h1>
	</header><!-- .entry-header -->

	<div class="entry-content">
		<p>Performance Studies Doctoral Program</p>
<p><strong>With whom do I speak with questions about the program?</strong><br />
You may contact Robin Davidson, head of Graduate Student Services. You can reach her at: 510-664-7613 (AM only) or <a href="mailto:performancestudies@berkeley.edu">performancestudies@berkeley.edu</a></p>
<p><strong>How do I know if I have to take the TOEFL?</strong><br />
Please read the information on the Graduate Division web site and application about <a href="http://grad.berkeley.edu/admissions/requirements/">admission requirements</a>.</p>
<p><strong>How important are GRE scores?</strong><br />
We do not consider GRE scores a primary indicator of success in a doctoral program, but we do take them into consideration. GREs are also reported when we nominate students for prestigious campus fellowships, so we do consider that factor during the admissions process. We don&#8217;t have a minimum score, but there are no exceptions or waivers for the GRE. Please note, scores must not be more than 5 years old as they are only reported for 5 years after taking the test. Specific information can be found on the <a href="http://www.ets.org/gre">GRE website</a>.</p>
<p><strong>How important are the writing samples?</strong><br />
Both personal statements and the Critical Writing Sample are very important. This is the place where the admissions committee will be best able to gauge a candidate&#8217;s readiness for doctoral research. Candidates should choose the critical writing sample that best exemplifies their critical capacities as theorists, historians, ethnographers, and/or as cultural critics. Ideally, the writing sample will be in dialogue with a candidate&#8217;s statement of research interests, though we understand that some candidates&#8217; &#8220;best&#8221; writing samples might be somewhat outside declared research interests. Candidates who have been away from academia for a while are encouraged to take the time to develop a new or revised well-researched and critically sophisticated writing sample. While the personal statements are fairly brief, the critical writing samples should ideally be around 15 to 20 pages.</p>
<p><strong>How important are letters of recommendation?</strong><br />
The letters of recommendation are very important. The letters should speak as best as possible to a candidate&#8217;s readiness for and interest in doctoral research. While one of three letters might speak to a candidate&#8217;s skills as an artist, administrator, or activist, at least two letters should speak knowledgeably about the candidate&#8217;s abilities as a researcher and writer.</p>
<p><strong>What kind of financial package is offered to doctoral students in performance studies?</strong><br />
We offer each student a five-year package of tuition support and stipend. The details of each package vary somewhat depending upon the availability of external campus funding and on the mix of fellowship and teaching responsibilities offered a student in any given year. However, we do not admit any student unless we can guarantee him or her a five-year package.</p>
<p><strong>Can any requirements be waived through work completed in my Masters program?</strong><br />
Not usually. The doctoral program in performance studies is rigorous and very specific to UC Berkeley. Many students enter our program with a Masters degree, however, and we find that such students are particularly adept in composing a specialized research curriculum and often take less time to finish their dissertations at the end of the program.</p>
<p><strong>Do you encourage students to take courses in departments outside of Theater, Dance, and Performance Studies?</strong><br />
Seminar experiences outside of the department are essential to the performance studies doctoral program at Berkeley. While the first year is largely devoted to program requirements in theory (201a/201b), methods (202), theory/practice experiments (203), and professional development (200a/200b), the rest of a student&#8217;s coursework is carefully selected from an array of courses offered on the Berkeley campus. Students meet regularly with the Head Graduate Advisor to craft a curriculum that best suits the research interests of the individual students, each of whom will be pursuing a research agenda that varies historically, regionally, theoretically, artistically, politically.</p>
<p><strong>What is the role of the Graduate Group faculty in Performance Studies?</strong><br />
The Graduate Group in Performance Studies is composed of scholarly faculty from within TDPS as well as a network of faculty whose work engages issues of performance from a variety of disciplinary angles. Graduate Group faculty rotate in two and three-year cycles onto the Executive Committee which is responsible for graduate admissions, curriculum decisions, and graduate student reviews. Graduate Group &#8220;affiliate&#8221; members regularly admit PS students into their courses and serve on their orals and dissertation committees. Graduate Group &#8220;core&#8221; members serve on the Executive Committee and can also serve as dissertation directors.</p>
<p><strong>Can I apply to the doctoral program if I have a BFA?</strong><br />
Some students are justifiably concerned that their undergraduate degree has not prepared them for doctoral research. In those cases, we encourage candidates to take interim steps through coursework or other kinds of intellectual affiliation to develop skills as a researcher and theorist.</p>
<p><strong>Can I apply to the doctoral program if my Bachelor&#8217;s degree is in a field other than Theater, Drama, Dance or Performance Studies?</strong><br />
Performance studies is a diverse and interdisciplinary field with scholarship representing a range of specialties in the humanities and social sciences, as well as occasionally the sciences. In light of this, a variety of undergraduate degrees are acceptable as long as the admissions statement includes a clear intention to pursue performance studies at the graduate level.</p>
<p><strong>Can I pursue a doctorate while living outside of the San Francisco Bay Area?</strong><br />
Because students take courses on campus for the first three years and teach regularly in the program, it is not possible to pursue our doctoral program on a commuter basis. In the summers and in the fourth or fifth years, students whose research requires national or international travel are certainly allowed to relocate for an appropriate period of time.</p>
<p><strong>Is there financial support for conference or research travel?</strong><br />
Students can receive Graduate Division support for two conferences during their time in our program and we can then help finance two or three additional conference trips.  The department also offers partial support for travel to facilitate doctoral research, usually after year 2 and again after years 4 or 5; allocations are made every year and depend upon the number of requests received. There are also other sources for travel funds throughout the campus as well as a variety of fellowship opportunities to support lengthier periods of research.</p>
<p><strong>Is it possible to pursue scholarly research in dance at UC Berkeley?</strong><br />
Yes. Dance Studies is an important aspect of our program and we currently have several students in residence who work in this field. In addition, several Graduate Group members publish on dance in the context of larger scholarly projects in contemporary performance, transnational performance, and popular, mass, or vernacular performance forms. Additionally, our choreographers are active in promoting dance studies, and some are very committed members of our Dance Studies Working Group, a multi-disciplinary scholarly group composed of faculty and graduate students in PS, Rhetoric, Art History, Digital Art, English, Anthropology, and more.</p>
<p><strong>What is the role of production in the performance studies doctoral program?</strong><br />
The doctorate program is designed to enable graduate students to become competitive in an academic job market, and we encourage students to participate in production to the degree that it advances their profiles as emerging scholars in performance studies. Our doctoral program is not an M.F.A. program. However, graduate students whose performance work coincides with their research have a variety of opportunities to cultivate their skills as artists, from the Performance Practicum class to courses in directing and performance art. After the first year, students can also apply to direct a Workshop production or to choreograph a piece for our Berkeley Dance Project.</p>
<p><strong>How can I contact a graduate faculty member?</strong><br />
The profiles, research interests, and contact information of our faculty are available on the website. After studying their biographies and research information, you can contact those whose interests are closest to yours. You can also contact the Head Graduate Advisor in Performance Studies, Professor Shannon Steen, steen21@berkeley.edu.</p>
<p><strong>Can I visit a seminar?</strong><br />
Visiting a seminar is something that occurs at the discretion of the professor; you can feel free to contact a professor about the possibility of visiting his or her course. Our course schedule is posted on the website.</p>
<p><strong>Can I speak with any current students in the program?</strong><br />
The profiles and research interests of our current graduate students are posted on our department website, along with their emails. After perusing their biographies, you can contact students, especially those whose interests are closest to yours.</p>
<p><strong>Is it possible for international students to take graduate courses at Berkeley?</strong><br />
International students are welcome to apply directly to the doctoral program. Those international students who wish to pursue graduate study at Berkeley for a limited time may apply through a number of programs:</p>
<p>Education Abroad Program (EAP) is an international educational program of the University of California that provides academic exchanges for one or two semesters.<br />
<a href="http://eap.ucop.edu/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://eap.ucop.edu</a></p>
<p>AMIDEAST Fulbright, America-Mideast Educational and Training Services, Inc., <a href="http://www.amideast.org" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://www.amideast.org</a></p>
<p>German and Portuguese Fulbright Commissions<br />
<a href="http://www.Fulbright.de" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://www.Fulbright.de</a><br />
<a href="http://www.ccla.pt" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://www.ccla.pt</a></p>
<p>Institute for International Education Fulbright<br />
<a href="http://www.iie.org" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://www.iie.org</a></p>
<p><strong>Is it possible for domestic students to take graduate courses at Berkeley?</strong><br />
Domestic students who want to undertake graduate study without working for a higher degree may apply for <strong>course-work-only status</strong>. They must, however, meet the same admission requirements as degree candidates, have a definite scholarly or professional purpose in applying, and be admitted to a regularly established major field of study. There is no limited or unclassified status available to graduate students. Course-work-only students do not qualify for fellowship consideration or for academic appointment as a Graduate Student Instructor and can be accommodated only if a department is willing to include them in its enrollment target. There is a maximum of two semesters of study. Admission to course-work-only status precludes all future admission to any degree program at UC Berkeley. Please see information on this website about graduate admission and the link to the application itself on the Graduate Division website.</p>
<p>Current graduate students from any UC campus, Stanford University, CSU East Bay, San Francisco State University, Mills College or Sonoma State University may participate in an <a href="http://grad.berkeley.edu/programs/exchange-programs/">Intercampus Exchange Program</a>. Check with your home campus for details. For those attending universities other than those mentioned above, check with your home campus to see if any kind of exchange may be arranged.</p>
	</div><!-- .entry-content -->
</article><!-- #post-560 -->
