<article id="post-260" class="group post-container">
	<header class="entry-header">
		<h1 class="entry-title">Dance &#038; Performance Studies Major</h1>
	</header><!-- .entry-header -->

	<div class="entry-content">
		<h2>CONTENTS</h2>
<p><a href="#Goals">1. Learning Goals</a><br />
<a href="#Path">2. Path to Achieving Goals</a><br />
<a href="#Evaluation">3. Statement of Methods of Evaluation and Feedback Mechanisms</a><br />
<a href="#Declare">4. Declaring the Major</a><br />
<a href="#Transfer">5. Things to Know About Transfer Credits</a><br />
<a href="#Contact">6. Contact Us</a><br />
<a id="Goals"></a><br />
&nbsp;</p>
<h2><strong>LEARNING GOALS</strong></h2>
<p>By the end of their time in Dance &amp; Performance Studies, students should possess:</p>
<ul>
<li>The ability to synthesize a well-organized argument from textual or other evidence and to express it in formal, written form</li>
<li>Proficiency in research methods (i.e. utilization of public and private archives, libraries, electronic databases, oral histories; textual and performance analysis)</li>
<li>Collaborative skills</li>
<li>Foundational stagecraft and production skills and knowledge (design, craft and technology, stage management, new media)</li>
<li>Literacy in foundational dramatic texts and fundamental concepts of performance theory</li>
<li>Basic knowledge of the history of Euro-American dance practice, including issues of race, ethnicity, and multiculturalism in the performing arts.</li>
<li>Basic modern/contemporary dance technique in the Western concert dance tradition</li>
<li>Understanding of the choreographic process and the tools necessary for this process.</li>
</ul>
<p>Through upper-division course work, electives, and capstone experiences students should also possess advanced training in at least one of the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Choreography</li>
<li>Advanced Dance Technique</li>
<li>History &amp; Theory of Dance</li>
</ul>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<h2><strong>PATH TO ACHIEVING GOALS</strong></h2>
<p>The path to achieving the aforementioned Learning Goals includes building Foundational Skills, developing Advanced Abilities and undertaking Capstone Experiences.</p>
<ul>
<li>FOUNDATIONAL SKILLS
<ul>
<li>Beginning Modern Dance Technique (40A/B)</li>
<li>Introduction to Performance Studies (26)</li>
<li>Stagecraft (60)</li>
<li><strong>EITHER</strong> Drama of American Cultures (Theater 25AC) <strong>OR </strong>Reflections of Gender, Culture and Ethnicity in Dance (52AC)</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>ADVANCED ABILITIES
<ul>
<li>Dance Technique: Once a declared major, students take technique classes every term at their appropriate level (Intermediate Modern Technique 141A/B, Advanced 1 Modern Technique 142A/B, or Advanced 2 Modern Technique 143A/B)</li>
<li>Performance Studies: Three courses from areas of Performance Theory, Performance History, Performance Literatures, or Performance and Culture</li>
<li>Technical Theater/Design: One lab requirement (167 or 168)<strong> AND</strong> one design requirement (Adv. Production Study 172, Scenic Design for the Theater 173A/B, Costume Design for the Theater 174A/B, Lighting Design for the Theater 175A/B, Sound Design 177, Music Resources for Performance 145)</li>
<li>Choreography Series: choose <strong>EITHER</strong> Sources of Movement 144 <strong>OR</strong> Performance Workshop 114 and Beginning Choreography 146A.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>CAPSTONE EXPERIENCES
<ul>
<li>Productions (from blackbox workshops to main stage productions)</li>
<li>Professional workshops and classes with Artists-in-Residence</li>
<li>Honors Theses (both written and production projects)</li>
<li>Independent Studies</li>
<li>Internships with professional companies, studios, agencies</li>
<li>Student-created performance projects</li>
<li>Leading/teaching DeCal courses</li>
<li>Research assistantships</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p><img class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-5237" src="http://tdps.berkeley.edu/files/2009/08/danceUSLIgraphic.jpg" alt="danceUSLIgraphic" width="651" height="724"><br />
<a id="Evaluation"></a><br />
&nbsp;</p>
<h2 style="text-align: left;"><strong>STATEMENT OF METHODS OF EVALUATION AND FEEDBACK MECHANISMS</strong></h2>
<p style="text-align: left;">In addition to traditional methods of assessment such as analytical papers, research projects, and examinations (which are used primarily in the Performance Studies courses), the TDPS faculty and lecturers use a variety of qualitative and competitive feedback methods. Among these are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Graded, Written, and Oral Assessment</li>
<li>Competitive Evaluation and Selection
<ul>
<li>Students compete with one another for limited spaces in classes and productions.</li>
<li>Those who work hard, perform well, and show promise in classes are provided increasing challenges and opportunities.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Distribution of prizes
<ul>
<li>Every year, the faculty distributes endowed awards to our students. These awards are given to students whom the faculty have known in both classes and productions, and who have been seen to excel in all areas of the curriculum. While production work is often the immediate anchor of these awards, academic achievement and good collaborative skills are also required of students who receive awards. Students lacking in either of these arenas can be disqualified from receiving awards.</li>
<li>These awards are the culmination of long-term assessment over the student’s time in TDPS. In other words, it is highly unlikely that a student will receive an award without having received extensive feedback leading up to that award.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>One-on-one mentorship and supervision
<ul>
<li>&nbsp;Students in choreography, dance technique, design, acting, directing, and stagecraft classes are encouraged (and often required) to solicit detailed assessment on particular projects from their faculty</li>
<li>For classes that require group projects, faculty give feedback to individual groups within a course, rather than one-on-one. However, these groups are generally small (4-6 students)</li>
<li>Students may ask for more detailed feedback on auditions from relevant directors or faculty</li>
<li>Guidance on written thesis</li>
<li>Supervision of internship or apprenticeship projects</li>
<li>Guidance through the major tailored to student’s long-term goals</li>
<li>Professional career feedback</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p><a id="Declare"></a><br />
&nbsp;</p>
<h2>DECLARING THE MAJOR</h2>
<p>Students may declare a major in TDPS after passing two pre-requisite courses</p>
<ul>
<li>one Modern Dance course (technique at any level in the Department) or Theater 60</li>
<li>one Performance Studies course (25AC or 26 or 52AC).</li>
</ul>
<p>Why declare early? This allows the best use of the many curricular and production opportunities offered by TDPS while at Cal. Additionally, majors are prioritized in decisions about enrollments, auditions, special offers, newsletter info, departmental awards, Main Stage subscriptions, design/choreographic/directing opportunities, and other department resources.</p>
<p><strong>To read about Dance &amp; Performance Studies Major Requirements: </strong><a href="http://guide.berkeley.edu/undergraduate/degree-programs/dance-performance-studies/#majorrequirementstext" target="_blank">Current requirements</a></p>
<p>You should also know that, as a major, it is expected that students will maintain a 2.0 GPA. Additionally, letter-graded courses for the major <strong>MUST</strong> be taken for a letter grade.</p>
<p>Please see the Department’s&nbsp;<a href="http://tdps.berkeley.edu/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/TDPSUndergraduateStudentHandbook2016-17.pdf">Undergraduate Handbook</a> for more information.<br />
<a id="Transfer"></a><br />
&nbsp;</p>
<h2>THINGS TO KNOW ABOUT TRANSFER CREDITS</h2>
<ul>
<li>A maximum of 8 units of equivalent coursework from EAP or other 4-year colleges transfer into the major as electives, upon departmental approval.</li>
<li>All L&amp;S-approved credits from other colleges transfer into your degree, but rarely into the major.</li>
<li>Transfer students should bring a copy of previous transcripts/course descriptions to Michael Mansfield for evaluation</li>
</ul>
<p><a id="Contact"></a><br />
&nbsp;</p>
<h2>CONTACT</h2>
<p><em>Academic questions, declare major, class schedule planning:</em></p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong>Michael Mansfield, Undergraduate Advisor</strong><br />
15B Dwinelle Hall &nbsp;(office hours: Mon-Fri, 1pm to 4pm)<br />
(510) 643-4050<br />
<a href="mailto:tdpsugadvisor@berkeley.edu">tdpsugadvisor@berkeley.edu</a></p>
<p><em>Resources, advice, career questions:</em></p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong>SanSan Kwan, Faculty Advisor for Dance</strong><br />
15F Dwinnell Hall<br />
sansankwan@berkeley.edu</p>
	</div><!-- .entry-content -->

<article id="post-264" class="group post-container">
	<header class="entry-header">
		<h1 class="entry-title">Dance &#038; Performance Studies Minor</h1>
	</header><!-- .entry-header -->

	<div class="entry-content">
		<h2>CONTENTS</h2>
<p><a href="#Confirm">1. Confirming the Minor</a><br />
<a href="#Requirements">2. Dance &amp; Performance Studies Minor Requirements</a><br />
<a href="#Samples">3. Sample Minor Tracks</a><br />
<a href="#Transfer">4. Things to Know About Transfer Credits</a><br />
<a href="#Contact">5. Contact Us</a><br />
<a id="Confirm"></a><br />
&nbsp;</p>
<h2><strong>CONFIRMING THE MINOR</strong></h2>
<p>Students can confirm their intention to <strong>minor</strong> in Theater &amp; Performance Studies after enrolling in <strong>one</strong> course in the Department of Theater, Dance, and Performance Studies.</p>
<p>Things to know about your minor:</p>
<ul>
<li>All courses in the minor must be taken for a letter-grade.</li>
<li>You must keep a GPA of 2.0 or better in the upper division minor units.</li>
<li>A course with the identical course number may only be counted twice toward the minor, and only 2 courses may be repeated in this way. (Exception: Intermediate Ballet for the Modern Dancer (Theater 147) may only count once toward the minor.)</li>
<li>See the Undergraduate Handbook for further information.</li>
</ul>
<p><a id="Requirements"></a><br />
&nbsp;</p>
<h2><strong>DANCE &amp; PERFORMANCE STUDIES MINOR REQUIREMENTS</strong></h2>
<p><strong>To read about Theater &amp; Performance Studies Minor Requirements: </strong><a href="http://guide.berkeley.edu/undergraduate/degree-programs/dance-performance-studies/#minorrequirementstext" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Current requirements</a></p>
<p>You should also know that, as a major, it is expected that students will maintain a 2.0 GPA. Additionally, letter-graded courses for the major <strong>MUST</strong> be taken for a letter grade.</p>
<p>Please see the Department’s&nbsp;<a href="http://tdps.berkeley.edu/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/TDPSUndergraduateStudentHandbook2016-17.pdf">Undergraduate Handbook</a> for more information.<br />
<a id="Samples"></a><br />
&nbsp;</p>
<h2>SAMPLE MINOR TRACKS</h2>
<p>The Theater &amp; Performance Studies Minor requires you to take four upper division electives that build a focus in your major. The sample minors provided below illustrate different potential focus areas, and are intended to help you imagine how you could build a unique focus of your own choosing. You <span style="color: #800000;"><strong>DO NOT</strong></span> have to choose one of these samples in order to minor in our department. We recommend you tailor your chosen electives to your personal interests.</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Sample: Minor with a Choreography Focus</span></strong><br />
40 Beginning Modern Dance<br />
141 Intermediate Modern Dance<br />
144 Sources for Movement<br />
146A Choreography<br />
146B Choreography<br />
125 Topics in Performance History</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><span style="text-decoration: underline;"><strong>Sample: Minor with a Performance Focus</strong></span><br />
40A Beginning Modern Dance<br />
141A Intermediate Modern Dance<br />
141B Intermediate Modern Dance<br />
144 Sources of Movement<br />
121 Topics in Performance Culture<br />
180 Dance Performance</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><span style="text-decoration: underline;"><strong>Sample: Minor with a Performance Studies Focus</strong></span><br />
40 Beginning Modern Dance<br />
114 Movement for the Theater<br />
119 Topics in Performance Theory<br />
125 Topics in Performance History<br />
126 Topics in Performance Literature<br />
122 Topics in Performance Culture</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><span style="text-decoration: underline;"><strong>Sample: Minor with a Technical Focus</strong></span><br />
60 Stagecraft<br />
141 Intermediate Modern Dance<br />
114 Movement for the Theater<br />
119 Topics in Performance Theory<br />
174 Costume Design<br />
179 Costume Production</p>
<p><a id="Transfer"></a><br />
&nbsp;</p>
<h2>THINGS TO KNOW ABOUT TRANSFER CREDIT</h2>
<ul>
<li>The Dance &amp; Performance Studies Minor requires five upper division courses; at least three of these courses must be taken in the Department.</li>
<li>A transferred course from another college or another department must be advisor-approved. Transfer students can determine transfer-ability of coursework into the minor by bringing a copy of previous transcripts/course descriptions to Michael Mansfield for evaluation.</li>
<li>Since your minor will be from the Department of Theater, Dance, and Performance Studies, it is likely you will do most of your minor coursework here.</li>
</ul>
<p><a id="Contact"></a><br />
&nbsp;</p>
<h2>CONTACT US</h2>
<p><em>Academic questions, declare major, class schedule planning:</em></p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong>Michael Mansfield, Undergraduate Advisor</strong><br />
15B Dwinelle Hall&nbsp;(office hours: Mon-Fri, 1pm to 4pm)<br />
(510) 643-4050<br />
<a href="mailto:tdpsugadvisor@berkeley.edu">tdpsugadvisor@berkeley.edu</a></p>
<p><em>Resources, advice, career questions:</em></p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong>SanSan Kwan, Faculty Advisor for Dance</strong><br />
15F Dwinnell Hall<br />
sansankwan@berkeley.edu</p>
	</div><!-- .entry-content -->
</article><!-- #post-264 -->

<article id="post-253" class="group post-container">
	<header class="entry-header">
		<h1 class="entry-title">Theater &#038; Performance Studies Major</h1>
	</header><!-- .entry-header -->

	<div class="entry-content">
		<h2>CONTENTS</h2>
<p><a href="#Goals">1. Learning Goals</a><br />
<a href="#Path">2. Path to Achieving Goals</a><br />
<a href="#Evaluation">3. Statement of Methods of Evaluation and Feedback Mechanisms</a><br />
<a href="#Declare">4. Declaring the Major</a><br />
<a href="#Transfer">5. Things to Know About Transfer Credits</a><br />
<a href="#Contact">6. Contact Us</a><br />
<a id="Goals"></a><br />
&nbsp;</p>
<h2><strong>LEARNING GOALS</strong></h2>
<p>By the end of their time in Theater &amp; Performance Studies, students should possess:</p>
<ul>
<li>The ability to synthesize a well-organized argument from textual or other evidence and to express it in formal, written form</li>
<li>Proficiency in research methods (i.e. utilization of public and private archives, libraries, electronic databases, oral histories; textual and performance analysis)</li>
<li>Collaborative skills</li>
<li>Foundational stagecraft and production skills and knowledge (design, craft and technology, stage management, new media)</li>
<li>Literacy in foundational dramatic texts and fundamental concepts of performance theory</li>
<li>Basic knowledge of the history of Euro-American theater practice, including issues of race, ethnicity, and multiculturalism in the performing arts.</li>
<li>Basic acting technique</li>
</ul>
<p>Through upper-division course work, electives, and capstone experiences students should also possess advanced training in at least one of the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Directing</li>
<li>Playwriting</li>
<li>Acting (Check out our <a href="http://tdps.berkeley.edu/wp-content/uploads/2013/09/Acting-Program-PDF.pdf">Acting Program</a>)</li>
<li>Design</li>
<li>History/Theory/Literature</li>
<li>Stage Management</li>
<li>New Media</li>
</ul>
<p>&nbsp;<br />
<a id="Path"></a><br />
&nbsp;</p>
<h2><strong>PATH TO ACHIEVING GOALS</strong></h2>
<p>The path to achieving the aforementioned Learning Goals includes building Foundational Skills, developing Advanced Abilities and undertaking Capstone Experiences.</p>
<ul>
<li>FOUNDATIONAL SKILLS
<ul>
<li>Introduction to Acting (Theater 10)</li>
<li>Introduction to Performance Studies (Theater 26)</li>
<li>Introduction to Technical Theater&nbsp;(Theater 60)</li>
<li><strong>EITHER</strong> Drama of American Cultures (Theater 25AC) <strong>OR </strong>Reflections of Gender, Culture and Ethnicity in Dance (Theater 52AC)</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>ADVANCED ABILITIES
<ul>
<li>Advanced Production or Design: participation in Studio&nbsp;or Playhouse&nbsp;productions</li>
<li>Performance Studies: Three courses from areas of Performance Theory, Performance History, Performance Literatures, or Performance and Culture</li>
<li>Four upper-division electives in student&#8217;s choice of area (directing, acting, design, etc.).</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>CAPSTONE EXPERIENCES
<ul>
<li>Productions (from Workshops to advanced participation in&nbsp;Playhouse productions)</li>
<li>Professional workshops and classes with Artists-in-Residence</li>
<li>Honors Theses (both written and production projects)</li>
<li>Independent Studies</li>
<li>Internships with professional companies, studios, agencies</li>
<li>Student-created performance projects</li>
<li>Leading/teaching DeCal courses</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p>&nbsp;<br />
<a id="Evaluation"></a><br />
&nbsp;</p>
<h2 style="text-align: left;"><strong>STATEMENT OF METHODS OF EVALUATION AND FEEDBACK MECHANISMS</strong></h2>
<p style="text-align: left;">In addition to traditional methods of assessment such as analytical papers, research projects, and examinations (which are used primarily in the Performance Studies courses), the TDPS faculty and lecturers use a variety of qualitative and competitive feedback methods. Among these are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Graded, Written, and Oral Assessment</li>
<li>Competitive Evaluation and Selection
<ul>
<li>Students compete with one another for limited spaces in classes and productions.</li>
<li>Those who work hard, perform well, and show promise in classes are provided increasing challenges and opportunities.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Distribution of prizes
<ul>
<li>Every year, the faculty distributes endowed awards to our students. These awards are given to students whom the faculty have known in both classes and productions, and who have been seen to excel in all areas of the curriculum. While production work is often the immediate anchor of these awards, academic achievement and good collaborative skills are also required of students who receive awards. Students lacking in either of these arenas can be disqualified from receiving awards.</li>
<li>These awards are the culmination of long-term assessment over the student’s time in TDPS. In other words, it is highly unlikely that a student will receive an award without having received extensive feedback leading up to that award.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>One-on-one mentorship and supervision
<ul>
<li>&nbsp;Students in choreography, dance technique, design, acting, directing, and stagecraft classes are encouraged (and often required) to solicit detailed assessment on particular projects from their faculty</li>
<li>For classes that require group projects, faculty give feedback to individual groups within a course, rather than one-on-one. However, these groups are generally small (4-6 students)</li>
<li>Students may ask for more detailed feedback on auditions from relevant directors or faculty</li>
<li>Guidance on written thesis</li>
<li>Supervision of internship or apprenticeship projects</li>
<li>Guidance through the major tailored to student’s long-term goals</li>
<li>Professional career feedback</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p>&nbsp;<br />
<a id="Declare"></a><br />
&nbsp;</p>
<h2 style="text-align: left;">DECLARING THE MAJOR</h2>
<p>Students may declare a major in TDPS after passing two pre-requisite courses: one Theater course (10 or 60) <strong>AND</strong> one Performance Studies course (25AC or 26 or 52AC).</p>
<p>Why declare early? This allows the best use of the many curricular and production opportunities offered by TDPS while at Cal. Additionally, majors are prioritized in decisions about enrollments, auditions, special offers, newsletter info, departmental awards, Main Stage subscriptions, design/choreographic/directing opportunities, and other department resources.</p>
<p><strong>To read about Theater &amp; Performance Studies Major Requirements: </strong><a href="http://guide.berkeley.edu/undergraduate/degree-programs/theater-performance-studies/#majorrequirementstext" target="_blank">Current requirements</a></p>
<p>You should also know that, as a major, it is expected that students will maintain a 2.0 GPA. Additionally, letter-graded courses for the major <strong>MUST</strong> be taken for a letter grade.</p>
<p>Please see the Department&#8217;s&nbsp;<a href="http://tdps.berkeley.edu/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/TDPSUndergraduateStudentHandbook2016-17.pdf">Undergraduate Handbook</a> for more information.<br />
&nbsp;<br />
<a id="Transfer"></a><br />
&nbsp;</p>
<h2>THINGS TO KNOW ABOUT TRANSFER CREDITS</h2>
<ul>
<li>A maximum of 8 units of equivalent coursework from EAP or other 4-year colleges transfer into the major as electives, upon departmental approval.</li>
<li>Equivalent courses to Theater 10 transfer into the major.</li>
<li>All L&amp;S-approved credits from other colleges transfer into your degree, but rarely into the major.</li>
<li>Transfer students should bring a copy of previous transcripts/course descriptions to Michael Mansfield for evaluation</li>
</ul>
<p>&nbsp;<br />
<a id="Contact"></a></p>
<h2>CONTACT</h2>
<p><em>Academic questions, declare major, class schedule planning:</em></p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong>Michael Mansfield, Undergraduate Advisor</strong><br />
15B Dwinelle Hall&nbsp;(office hours: Mon-Fri, 1pm to 4pm)<br />
(510) 643-4050<br />
<a href="mailto:tdpsugadvisor@berkeley.edu">tdpsugadvisor@berkeley.edu</a></p>
<p><em>Resources, advice, career questions:</em></p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong>Abigail De Kosnik, Faculty Advisor for Theater</strong><br />
<a href="mailto:mgordon@berkeley.edu">adekosnik@berkeley.edu</a></p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong>SanSan Kwan, Faculty Advisor for Dance</strong><br />
<a title="BareStage – MACBETH &amp; 2014/2015 APPLICATIONS" href="mailto:lisawymore@berkeley.edu">sansankwan@berkeley.edu</a></p>

<article id="post-256" class="group post-container">
	<header class="entry-header">
		<h1 class="entry-title">Theater &#038; Performance Studies Minor</h1>
	</header><!-- .entry-header -->

	<div class="entry-content">
		<h2>CONTENTS</h2>
<p><a href="#Confirm">1. Confirming the Minor</a><br />
<a href="#Requirements">2. Theater &amp; Performance Studies Minor Requirements</a><br />
<a href="#Samples">3. Sample Minor Tracks</a><br />
<a href="#Transfer">4. Things to Know About Transfer Credits</a><br />
<a href="#Contact">5. Contact Us</a><br />
<a id="Confirm"></a><br />
&nbsp;</p>
<h2><strong>CONFIRMING THE MINOR</strong></h2>
<p>Students can confirm their intention to <strong>minor</strong> in Theater &amp; Performance Studies after enrolling in <strong>one</strong> course in the Department of Theater, Dance, and Performance Studies.</p>
<p>Things to know about your minor:</p>
<ul>
<li>All courses in the minor must be taken for a letter-grade.</li>
<li>You must keep a GPA of 2.0 or better in the upper division minor units.</li>
<li>A course with the identical course number may only be counted twice toward the minor, and only 2 courses may be repeated in this way.</li>
<li>See the Undergraduate Handbook for further information.</li>
</ul>
<p><a id="Requirements"></a><br />
&nbsp;</p>
<h2><strong>THEATER &amp; PERFORMANCE STUDIES MINOR REQUIREMENTS</strong></h2>
<p><strong>To read about Theater &amp; Performance Studies Minor Requirements: </strong><a href="http://guide.berkeley.edu/undergraduate/degree-programs/theater-performance-studies/#minorrequirementstext" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Current requirements</a></p>
<p>You should also know that, as a major, it is expected that students will maintain a 2.0 GPA. Additionally, letter-graded courses for the major <strong>MUST</strong> be taken for a letter grade.</p>
<p>Please see the Department’s&nbsp;<a href="http://tdps.berkeley.edu/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/TDPSUndergraduateStudentHandbook2016-17.pdf">Undergraduate Handbook</a> for more information.<br />
<a id="Samples"></a><br />
&nbsp;</p>
<h2>SAMPLE MINOR FOCUSES</h2>
<p>The Theater &amp; Performance Studies Minor requires you to take four upper division electives that build a focus in your major. The sample minors provided below illustrate different potential focus areas, and are intended to help you imagine how you could build your own unique focus. You <span style="color: #800000;"><strong>DO NOT</strong></span> have to choose one of these samples in order to minor in our department. We recommend you tailor your chosen electives to your personal interests.</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Sample: Minor with a Directing Focus </span></strong><br />
10 Beginning Acting<br />
110A Intermediate Acting*<br />
110B Intermediate Acting<br />
162 Directing 1<br />
163 Directing 2<br />
125 Topics in Performance History</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Sample: Minor with a Performance Studies Focus</span></strong><br />
26 Introduction to Performance Studies<br />
166 Special Topics in Performance<br />
125 Topics in Performance History<br />
126 Topics in Performance Literature<br />
122 Topics in Performance Culture</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Sample: Minor with an Acting Focus</span> (Check out our <a href="http://tdps.berkeley.edu/files/2013/09/Acting-Program-PDF.pdf">Acting Program</a>)</strong><br />
10 Beginning Acting<br />
110A Intermediate Acting*<br />
110B Intermediate Acting<br />
126 Topics in Performance Literature<br />
111 Advanced Acting<br />
111 Advanced Acting</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><span style="text-decoration: underline;"><strong>Sample: Minor with a Performance Focus</strong></span><br />
10 Beginning Acting<br />
110A Intermediate Acting*<br />
110B Intermediate Acting<br />
114 Performance Workshop<br />
121 Topics in Performance Culture<br />
181 Theater Performance</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><span style="text-decoration: underline;"><strong>Sample: Minor with a Technical Focus</strong></span><br />
60 Stagecraft<br />
173A Set Design<br />
173B Set Design<br />
119 Topics in Performance Theory<br />
179 Set Designer for a Show<br />
179 Set Designer for a Show</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><span style="text-decoration: underline;"><strong>Other samples could include:</strong></span><br />
Minor with a Stage Management focus<br />
Minor with a Costume Design Focus<br />
Minor with a Lighting Design Focus<br />
Minor with a Sound Design Focus</p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">*There is no assurance that you can jump directly from Theater 10 to Theater 110A, except by audition; a minor may also need to take Theater 109 before advancing to Theater 110A.</p>
<p>&nbsp;<br />
<a id="Transfer"></a><br />
&nbsp;</p>
<h2>THINGS TO KNOW ABOUT TRANSFER CREDIT</h2>
<ul>
<li>The Theater &amp; Performance Studies Minor requires five upper division courses; at least three of these courses must be taken in the Department.</li>
<li>A transferred course from another college or another department must be advisor-approved. Transfer students can determine transfer-ability of coursework into the minor by bringing a copy of previous transcripts/course descriptions to Michael Mansfield for evaluation.</li>
<li>Equivalent courses to Theater 10 transfer into the minor from other institutions.</li>
<li>Except for Theater 10, it is rare that a course from a Junior College will transfer into the minor because equivalent coursework is seldom found.</li>
<li>Since your minor will be from the Department of Theater, Dance, and Performance Studies, it is likely you will do most of your minor coursework here.</li>
</ul>
<p><a id="Contact"></a><br />
&nbsp;</p>
<h2>CONTACT US</h2>
<p><em>Academic questions, declare major, class schedule planning:</em></p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong>Michael Mansfield, Undergraduate Advisor</strong><br />
15B Dwinelle Hall &nbsp;(office hours: Mon-Fri, 1pm to 4pm)<br />
(510) 643-4050<br />
<a href="mailto:tdpsugadvisor@berkeley.edu">tdpsugadvisor@berkeley.edu</a></p>
<p><em>Resources, advice, career questions:</em></p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;"><strong>Abigail De Kosnik, Faculty Advisor for Theater</strong><br />
<a href="mailto:mgordon@berkeley.edu">adekosnik@berkeley.edu</a></p>
	</div><!-- .entry-content -->
</article><!-- #post-256 -->

			<div class="content page" role="main">

				
					
<article id="post-268" class="group post-container">
	<header class="entry-header">
		<h1 class="entry-title">Undergrad FAQs</h1>
	</header><!-- .entry-header -->

	<div class="entry-content">
		<p><strong>Why is the Department called Theater, Dance, and Performance Studies?</strong></p>
<p>Our discipline has changed as an artistic practice and as an academic field in the last two decades. Our Department changed its name in 1999 in order to reflect our commitment to offering the best mix of our field&#8217;s traditional history and its contemporary innovations. The term &#8220;Theater&#8221; marks all of our efforts to support the study and practice of the theatrical event, not only as a form of dramatic literature, but also as an imagistic, gestural, auditory, spatial, and technically complex project. While we have had a dance program for much of our history, the term &#8220;Dance&#8221; was only recently added to the official name, foregrounding dance practice and dance history as a central player in our Department&#8217;s self-definition. And finally, the term &#8220;Performance Studies&#8221; signals our relationship to one of the most fundamental alterations in the way scholars have re-imagined the &#8220;interdisciplinary&#8221; nature of performance. As artists increasingly draw from a range of media&#8211;crossing dance and theater, film and dance, theater and new technology&#8211;performance studies reflects a commitment to exposing our students to a range of artistic genres. As artists and scholars increasingly imagine themselves in relation to a variety of global and popular performance forms&#8211;thinking about the social role of carnivals and festivals, of television and rock concerts, of protests and raves&#8211;performance studies reflects our commitment to asking students to see their work in relation to a variety of performance forms in our culture and around the world.</p>
<p><strong>Why do we encourage the Dance majors and Theater majors to study together?</strong></p>
<p>We feel that today&#8217;s artistic climate requires a range of artistic skills and a facility between and amongst genres. Additionally, our requirements in history, literature, culture, and theory offer a chance for performers in different sub-fields to see themselves in relation to longer and wider traditions of performance experiment, an experience that reflects on the work of both theater and dance practitioners.</p>
<p><strong>Do you have to audition to get into the Theater and Performance Studies or Dance and Performance Studies Majors?</strong></p>
<p>No. Once you are accepted in UC Berkeley, you may study in any department. You are required to take some pre-requisites (a dance/theater course and a performance studies course) before declaring your major. This is to reassure you (and the Department) that you will be able to handle the technical and intellectual work of the coursework. You do audition for individual acting or dance classes each semester, and you do audition to be cast in specific shows or concerts.</p>
<p><strong>How do the TDPS undergraduate programs rank in comparison to other theater/dance programs?</strong></p>
<p>Our Department is most noted for its critical studies, its cross-disciplinary experimental stage work, and its productions related to social action. It is also known for housing a leading doctoral program in our field and for placing undergraduates in leading M.F.A. programs. </p>
<p>Beyond that, there are no standard rankings for theater/dance programs at American universities. In part, this has to do with the relatively small sizes of most programs and the difficulty of standardizing quality. Even word-of-mouth reputation can be outdated since so many university acting programs that began in the 1960s no longer have the faculty or exact fields of study that established their fame (we could claim Gregory Peck as a one-time acting student but that was in 1938). We are proud to promote cross-disciplinary performance practice and scholarship at one of the leading research universities in the world.</p>
<p><strong>How many students are in the Department?</strong></p>
<p>100 Theater Majors and 100 Theater Minors; 50 Dance Majors and 50 Dance Minors</p>
<p><strong>Can I take classes if I&#8217;m not a major?</strong></p>
<p>Yes, our courses are open to non-majors, though many fill quite quickly. Some practical classes do require auditions; other over-subscribed courses do give preference to majors.</p>
<p><strong>I&#8217;m a junior transfer and I&#8217;d like to major in the Department. Am I too late?</strong></p>
<p>No. You can easily fulfill the requirements for the Dance and Performance Studies Major or the Theater and Performance Studies Major in 4 semesters.</p>
<p><strong>I&#8217;ve already taken a lot of the requirements for the theater major at my previous junior college, 4-year college, or abroad, so do I have to take them again here?</strong></p>
<p>Most all of the units you have taken will transfer into UCB into your degree from the College of Letters and Science. The only course that regularly transfers into the major, however, is your beginning acting course, taken at a community college or 4-year college. If you took other courses in a 4-year college or abroad, you may transfer into the major up to 8 units of elective credit with courses that are comparable to or complementary to the courses offered here at TDPS. These courses will need to be approved by the Undergraduate Advisor, Faculty Advisor, or the Faculty Member teaching the comparable course.</p>
<p><strong>What do the students do with a theater or dance degree after they graduate? How successful are they?</strong></p>
<p>Some go directly into MFA programs, such as Yale School of Drama, NYU, or Northwestern University; others decide to enter a Theater Studies Ph.D. Program, such as those found at UC Berkeley, Stanford, Northwestern, New York University, or many others throughout the world. Some move to New York, Los Angeles, or San Francisco to work as actors, dancers, directors, designers, technicians, or by starting their own group or production company. Others move to Hollywood to work in the film and television community in front of or behind the camera. Still others go into a variety of professions in the social, corporate, legal, and arts sectors. We are proud of the ways our graduates have used their critical and expressive skills toward successful careers as professional artists in dance, theater, and experimental performance as well as in law, advertising, human resources, publishing, radio, technology, social work, and in all aspects of non-profit and business administration. For a snap-shot of the recent work of our alumni, we invite you to take a look out our annual newsletter and the alumni section of our website.</p>
<p><strong>How can I get connected or stay connected to the Department?</strong></p>
<p>TDPS students receive regular email updates from the Department with the most current information on auditions, course enrollments, productions, special events and lectures, ticket offers, internships, career opportunities, and more. If you would like to be on the mailing list, send your email address to tdpsugadvisor@berkeley.edu, requesting to be on the email list.</p>
<h2>ACADEMIC QUESTIONS</h2>
<p><strong>Do you have an UG Handbook for the Majors?</strong></p>
<p>Yes, you can download a pdf of our <a href="http://tdps.berkeley.edu/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/TDPSUndergraduateStudentHandbook2016-17.pdf">UndergraduateHandbook</a>.&nbsp;We strongly recommend that you read this manual thoroughly, as it offers detailed answers to some of the most important frequently-asked questions.</p>
<p><strong>Do you have any helpful documents that will help me plan my time in TDPS, or show pathways to focuses within the major such as Acting, Directing, Playwriting, Choreography, Stage Management, Design, etc?</strong></p>
<p>Yes, please see the Curriculum of Advising document below, giving examples of possible courses of study.</p>
<p><a href="http://tdps.berkeley.edu/wp-content/uploads/2013/09/Curriculum-of-Advising-PDF-Sheet1.pdf">Possible Course of Study for 4 Years or 4 Semesters in TDPS to Maximize Your Experience and Learning</a></p>
<p><strong>Can I meet with an advisor to talk about my studies in your Department?</strong></p>
<p>Yes, Michael Mansfield is our Undergraduate Advisor and is available by appointment in the Hearst Field Annex office Monday-Friday, 1-4pm. Professor Mel Gordon is our Head Undergraduate Advisor on the faculty. We strongly recommend that you thoroughly read the Undergraduate Handbook and relative information on our website before making an appointment with any staff or faculty member.</p>
<p><strong>How large are the TDPS classes?</strong></p>
<p>The Department is committed to keeping the theater, dance, and technical training courses to 20 students or less in a conservatory model. Performance studies courses may be larger due to their lecture format, but are often connected with smaller discussion sections of 20 or less.</p>
<p><strong>I&#8217;m a playwright/director/choreographer. Are there chances for me to create my own show within the Department?</strong></p>
<p>Yes. We have a number of opportunities for student-written, student-directed, and student-choreographed work to receive departmental support. These student-initiated shows in the departmental season are awarded competitively after review of formal proposals. If you&#8217;re interested in submitting a proposal for a student-written or student-directed work, we strongly encourage you to speak with a faculty supervisor as soon as possible so that you may submit a strong proposal to the evaluating committee. Performance-based proposals are due in February each year. Also see another two-semester option for proposing your own work in the following Honors Thesis question.</p>
<p><a href="http://tdps.berkeley.edu/wp-content/uploads/2009/08/196-Project-Application13-14.pdf">Theater 196 Student Directing or Choreography Project Application</a></p>
<p><strong>Does the Department have an Honors Thesis?</strong></p>
<p>Yes. The Honors Thesis is not a requirement for graduation, but rather an opportunity for a student to deepen their research with a project of particular interest to them. Students may apply to complete a year-long Honors Thesis project. It may take two forms: a year-long research project (a semester of research followed by a semester culminating in a full-length paper or written creation/play) or a semester of research and shorter research paper followed by a semester culminating in a creative project/production/show. Most Honors Theses begin in the fall and conclude in the spring. If a student will graduate in December instead, they may begin a written-only Honors Thesis in spring semester and conclude in the fall of the following academic year. Performance-based proposals are due the February before the two-semester commitment. Please see the Undergraduate Student Advisor if you have any questions regarding your proposal, and see below for an application.</p>
<p><a href="http://tdps.berkeley.edu/wp-content/uploads/2009/08/195-Honors-Thesis-or-Project-Application13-14.pdf">Theater 195 Honors Thesis Application</a></p>
<p><strong>Does the Department have internship opportunities?</strong></p>
<p>Yes. Many students have completed unpaid, off-campus internships for departmental credit at theater companies, television stations, etc. You will need to choose a faculty member to be your supervisor for this course and fill out the application form by the 12th week of the semester before the internship is scheduled to begin. Check with the UG Advisor or faculty for help in locating possible internships. Other pre-requisites of this course exist and are explained in the application form, which can be found below.</p>
<p><a href="http://tdps.berkeley.edu/wp-content/uploads/2009/08/197-Internship-Application.pdf">Theater 197 Internship Application</a></p>
<p><strong>Does the Department offer opportunities for me to teach a course while I am here?</strong></p>
<p>DeCal courses offer students the chance to propose teaching something that they have trained in or feel passionate about. Students may propose a course, and if approved, will work with a faculty member to create a course description, syllabus, and semester-long class. Application forms are due the 8th week of the semester before the DeCal course is scheduled to begin. Check with the UG Advisor or faculty for help in creating possible DeCal courses. Other pre-requisites of this course exist and are explained in the application form. Please see below for Theater 98/198 DeCal Course Application.</p>
<p><a href="http://tdps.berkeley.edu/wp-content/uploads/2009/08/98-198-DeCal-Application13-14.pdf">Theater 98/198 DeCal Application</a></p>
<p><strong>Does the Department have independent study opportunities?</strong></p>
<p>Yes. Students may create an independent study proposal with any faculty member and fill out the application form by the 12th week of the semester before the independent study is scheduled to begin. Other pre-requisites of this course exist and are explained in the application form for Theater 199, which can be found below.</p>
<p><a href="http://tdps.berkeley.edu/wp-content/uploads/2009/08/99-199-Independent-Study-Application.pdf">Theater 99, 199 Independent Study Application</a></p>
<p><strong>Do I have to perform in shows to get a Theater and Performance Studies major?</strong></p>
<p>No, you do not have to perform to fulfill all of the participations required of the major. You can opt to participate in a variety of other ways (technical, design, directorial, etc.). For more specific questions regarding production rules and opportunities, see the Production FAQ section of our website.</p>
<h2>DANCE-RELATED QUESTIONS</h2>
<p><strong>What kind of dance do you teach?</strong></p>
<p>The Dance and Performance Studies Major is focused on modern/contemporary dance technique, choreography, performance, and research. We also offer a course in Ballet for the Contemporary Dancer, and Afro-Haitian Dance. Other dance courses (ballet, tap, jazz, folkdance, hiphop, ballroom, and modern) are offered in the Physical Education Department, but these courses are not connected with the Dance and Performance Studies Major. They are, however, wonderful complementary trainings to your work here in the Department. Excellent ballet courses are also available through Berkeley Ballet School, Oakland Ballet School, and San Francisco Ballet Academy.</p>
<p><strong>Do I need to prepare anything for the dance technique class auditions?</strong></p>
<p>No preparation is necessary. The audition for each dance technique class is the first class. If you have footless tights and leotards or tight fitting clothes, please wear them (there are changing rooms in the studio). You will be given a technique class by the instructor of that class and evaluated by that teacher in consultation with a panel from the dance faculty. You must audition for the level class in which you seek placement. You may audition for several classes if you are unsure of your abilities or level. Generally, 70% of the students auditioning are accepted.</p>
<p><strong>What are distinguishing characteristics of the Dance and Performance Studies Major?</strong></p>
<p>Dance programs are generally identified by particular characteristics. Berkeley&#8217;s program is unique in that 1) it is small, 2) it demands intensive commitment to the technical training, 3) it provides many opportunities for self-initiated and group-initiated creative dance projects, and 4) it fosters an intellectual grasp of the many issues associated with the world of modern/contemporary dance. The foundation is four levels of daily modern technique that build core strength and develop alignment. The program offers a three-semester creative cycle of courses that lead a student into Department-sponsored independent choreographic projects. Additionally, the Department provides numerous performance opportunities each year to its students. Choreographers for these projects may be guest professionals, faculty, or students. We are fortunate to be able to draw on the wealth of Bay Area dance teachers and choreographers for our studio classes. Performance Studies courses include the study of the history of dance, world dance forms, and the broader study of performance with movement being one of several media. The dance faculty is particularly interested in the development of conceptually-founded multi-disciplinary projects.</p>
	</div><!-- .entry-content -->
</article><!-- #post-268 -->

				
			</div><!-- #content -->
		</div><!-- #content-container -->

<article id="post-9115" class="group post-container">
	<header class="entry-header">
		<h1 class="entry-title">UC Berkeley Department of Theater, Dance and Performance Studies Installs State-of-the-Art Meyer Sound System</h1>
	</header><!-- .entry-header -->

	<div class="entry-content">
		
			
		<p>The <b>UC Berkeley Department of Theater, Dance and Performance Studies</b> (TDPS) has partnered with Berkeley-based <b>Meyer Sound</b> to install a state-of-the-art audio system in the 550-seat <b>Zellerbach Playhouse. </b>Used by both TDPS and Cal Performances, the newly-installed <b>Meyer Sound System</b> will provide optimal acoustics for a broad range of events, including theatrical performance, dance concerts, lectures, workshops, classes and special events.</p>
<p>Generously underwritten by Bay Area sound innovators Meyer Sound, the audio solution includes UPJunior-XP VariO loudspeakers, UP-4XP loudspeakers, UMS-1P and 500-HP subwoofers, and a Galileo loudspeaker management system for system drive and alignment. Meyer Sound equipment has also been installed in TDPS’s other performance and studio spaces, including the 140-seat Durham Studio Theater and the Zellerbach Room 7 blackbox.</p>
<p>“The old audio system in The Playhouse had been in operation for more than 30 years and was still functional, but did not offer an optimal sound experience,” says Wil Leggett, TDPS’s Production Manager. “Sound is an essential component of any theatrical experience. We want to offer the best experience possible to our students and our audiences, so when we had the opportunity to upgrade our system we went to Meyer Sound, a company that is the gold standard in professional audio equipment and also happens to be local.”</p>
<p>With the installation of Meyer Sound equipment, TDPS students have enhanced opportunities for hands-on work with precise professional audio, allowing for invaluable professional training and artistic growth. Chair of TDPS Catherine Cole says, “Meyer Sound equipment is renowned for accuracy and precision, and this new system will be an incredible asset to the student performers and designers that create in our spaces, the professional designers we hire, and the audiences that come through our doors—both now and for years to come.”</p>
<p>Based in Berkeley, Meyer Sound is a valued and generous community partner to UC Berkeley. In addition to the custom-designed TDPS system, Meyer Sound equipment provides memorable experiences at Zellerbach Hall, Memorial Stadium, Haas Pavilion and the new UC Berkeley Art Museum and Pacific Film Archive building. “With this state-of-the-art audio system from Meyer Sound, TDPS now has equipment on par with some of the best cultural institutions in the region and around the world,” says Cole.</p>
<p><b>ABOUT MEYER SOUND</b></p>
<p>Meyer Sound is a leader in the world of sound, continually seeking to elevate the overall dialogue about sound and bring greater awareness to the importance of how we hear and how we listen. Founded in 1979 by John and Helen Meyer, Meyer Sound has continually explored the everyday impact of sound—applying the highest level of scientific and acoustical principles to achieve extraordinary results in places ranging from restaurants to cruise ships to office space and concert halls and cathedrals. Outstanding design, manufacturing, service and support are the result of a company philosophy where creative thinking, old-fashioned craftsmanship and forward thinking technology are strongly intertwined.</p>
<p><b>ABOUT TDPS</b></p>
<p>Currently celebrating its 75th Anniversary, the UC Berkeley Department of Theater, Dance and Performance Studies teaches performance as a mode of critical inquiry, creative expression and public engagement. Through performance training and research, we create liberal arts graduates with expanded analytical, technical and imaginative capacities. As a public institution, we make diversity and inclusion a key part of our teaching, art making and public programming.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p>Spring 2016.</p>
			</div><!-- .entry-content -->
